Drunkard's Confession and Apostasy: Hadd and Marriage Effect
Ruling on drunkard's confession for hudud and effect of apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal effect of a drunkard's confession for huquq Allah vs. huquq al-'ibad, and state the effect of his apostasy on marriage according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A drunkard's confession averts hadd (haqq Allah) but establishes haqq al-'abd; his apostasy is ineffective—marriage remains intact.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the drunkard's confession is treated differently depending on whether the punishment is a pure right of God (haqq Allah) or involves a personal right (haqq al-'abd). The same distinction applies to apostasy—a matter of belief that cannot coexist with intoxication. We will unpack the reasoning behind these rulings and the intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
Locate the two separate issues: (1) the drunkard's confession for an act warranting hadd, and (2) the drunkard's apostasy. Note the different outcomes.
The passage moves from confession to apostasy; they are connected by the state of drunkenness.
2
Analyse the distinction in confession rulings
Understand why hadd (pure haqq Allah) is averted by doubt (increased possibility of falsehood), while hadd qadhf (involving haqq al-'abd) is enforced against the drunkard like the sober person.
Key principle: dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat applies only to pure huquq Allah.
3
Trace the proof for apostasy ruling
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that apostasy is a matter of belief (i'tiqad), which requires sound intellect; drunkenness negates that capacity, so apostasy is ineffective.
Contrast with other transactions (divorce, manumission) which are effective from a drunkard because they are actions, not beliefs.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and tarjih
Zahir al-Riwayah holds apostasy effective, drawing analogy to other valid transactions. The author prefers Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view, making it the mufta bihi.
This shows how later Hanafi authorities weigh differing transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَانُ بِإِقْرَارِهِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ لِزِيَادَةِ اِحْتِمَالِ الْكِذْبِ فِي إِقْرَارِهِ فَيُحْتَالُ لِدَرْئِهِ لِأَنَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِخِلَافِ حَدِ الْقَذَفِ إِنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّ الْعَبْدِ وَ السَّكْرَانُ فِيهِ كَالصَّاحِى عُقُوبَةٌ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ تَصَرُّفَاتِهِ وَلَوِ ارْتَدَّ السَّكْرَانُ لَا تَبِينُ مِنْهُ امْرَأَتُهُ لأَنَّ الْكُفْرَ مِنْ بَابِ الْاعْتِقَادِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعَ السُّكْرِ وَهِذَا قَولُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَفِي ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ تَكُونُ رِدَّةٍ

ترجمہ اگرنشہ میں مست شخص نے اپنے اوپر شراب کے پینے وغیرہ کا اعتراف کر لیا تو اس پر حد جاری نہیں کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کے اس اقرار میں جھوٹ کا زیادہ احتمال رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر سے حد کو دور کرنے کے لئے صلہ معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ حد تو خالص حق الہی ہے۔ بخلاف جد قذف کے کیونکہ اس سے بندہ کا حق متعلق ہوتا ہے اور ایسے حقوق عبد میں وہ سب برابر ہوتے ہیں جو نشہ میں مست ہوں یا جو ہوش و حواس سب میں ہوں۔ تا کہ نشہ میں مست اپنی پوری سزا پائے۔ جیسے کہ اس کے دوسرے تصرفات اور معاملات طلاق واعتاق وغیرہ اس پر نافذ کر دیئے جاتے ہیں۔ لیکن اگر ایسا شخص یعنی نشہ میں مست مرتد ہو جائے تو اس کی بیوی اس سے مطلقہ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایک اعتقادی معاملہ ہے۔ اس لئے نشہ کے ساتھ اس کا متحقق نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ اور امام محمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا ہے لیکن ظاہر الروایۃ میں وہ مرتد ہو جائے گا۔ (لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کو چھوڑ کر قول اول ہی مختار ہے)۔ ... و لا يحد السكران باقراره على نفسه لزيادة احتمال الكذب ... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
The drunkard is not punished by hadd upon his confession against himself due to the increased probability of falsehood in his confession, so a stratagem is sought to avert it because it is pure right of Allah, contrary to the hadd of qadhf because it contains the right of the slave; and the drunkard in it is like the sober person, a punishment upon him as in his other transactions. And if the drunkard apostatizes, his wife does not become separated from him because disbelief is a matter of belief, so it cannot be realized with drunkenness. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And in the apparent (zahir) transmission, it is considered apostasy.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct rulings. First, a drunkard's confession to an act warranting hadd (e.g., drinking wine) is not accepted because the likelihood of falsehood (due to impaired judgment) is high. Since hadd is a pure right of God, it can be averted by doubts. In contrast, the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery) involves a personal right (haqq al-'abd); therefore, the drunkard's confession is accepted as valid, just like the transactions of divorce and manumission which are effective from a drunkard to prevent him from escaping punishment. Second, regarding apostasy: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that a drunkard's apostasy is ineffective because apostasy is a matter of belief, which cannot coexist with the loss of intellect (drunkenness). Thus, his marriage remains intact. However, the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon transmission) considers it effective apostasy; but the author notes that the first view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the chosen (mukhtar) position for fatwa.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment; here specifically for wine drinking or qadhf.
حق الله (haqq Allah): Right of Allah; cannot be waived by individuals, averted by doubts.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): Right of the individual; can be established by confession of a drunkard.
ارتداد (irtidad): Apostasy from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the effect of a drunkard's apostasy on his marriage?
A) His wife becomes divorced immediately.
B) The marriage remains valid.
C) The marriage is suspended until he sobers.
D) The apostasy nullifies the marriage after three menstrual cycles.

Key Takeaway
A drunkard's confession is ineffective for hadd (pure haqq Allah) but effective for personal rights; his apostasy does not dissolve marriage because it is a matter of belief.

Conditions for Hadd al-Qadhf (False Accusation of Adultery)
Introduces the chapter on qadhf and states conditions for eighty lashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required for the execution of hadd al-qadhf and explain the Quranic proof for the ruling.

Core Idea
Eighty lashes for false accusation of zina require: explicit accusation, muhsan victim, and victim's demand.

The hadd of qadhf protects personal honor from false accusations of adultery. This lesson unpacks the conditions that must be met for this punishment to be applied, based on the Quranic command in Surah An-Nur. Understanding these conditions ensures that the hadd is not misapplied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is false accusation of zina (qadhf). The ruling is that the accuser receives eighty lashes if free (forty if slave).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (24:4) is cited: 'And those who accuse chaste women... then flog them eighty lashes.' This is the primary evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fajliduhum' (flog them) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The verse links the hadd to the failure to produce four witnesses for zina.
4
Note the conditions mentioned
The text explicitly requires: (1) explicit accusation of zina, (2) the accused is muhsan (free, adult, sane, Muslim, chaste), (3) the accused demands the hadd (mutalaba), and (4) the accuser is free for the full 80 lashes.
The condition of mutalaba is derived from the victim's personal right to clear honor.
5
Apply to a scenario
If any condition is missing, the hadd is not applied. For example, if the victim does not demand punishment, the accuser is not flogged; instead, he may face ta'zir if the victim sues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد القذف
ترجمہ باب ، زنا کا بہتان لگانا
حد قذف کا حکم

وَإِذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا أَوْ امْرَأَةً مُحْصَنَةً بِصَرِيحِ الزَّنَاءِ وَطَالَبَ الْمَقْذُوفُ بِالْحَدِّ حَدَّهُ الْحَاكِمُ ثَمَانِينَ سَوْطًا إِنْ كَانَ حُرًّا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ إِلَى أَنْ قَالَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً الْآيَةُ وَالْمُرَادُ الرَّمْيُ بِالزِّنَاءِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَفِي النَّصِّ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَيْهِ وَهُوَ اشْتِرَاطُ أَرْبَعَةٍ مِنَ الشُّهَدَاءِ إِذْ هُوَ مُخْتَصٌّ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَيُشْتَرَطُ مُطَالَبَةُ الْمَقْذُوفِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّهُ. حَيْثُ يَدْفَعُ الْعَارَ وَ إِحْصَانُ الْمَقْذُوفِ لِمَا تَلَوْنَا
Chapter of the Hadd of Qadhf. When a man accuses a chaste (muhsan) man or a chaste (muhsan) woman of explicit zina, and the accused demands the hadd, the judge flogs him eighty lashes if he is free, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who accuse chaste women... then flog them eighty lashes' (24:4). And what is meant by the verse, by consensus, is accusation of zina. And in the text there is an indication to it, which is the condition of four witnesses, since it is specific to zina. And the demand of the accused is required because it involves his right, by which he wards off shame. And the condition of the accused being muhsan is as we have recited.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of adultery). The ruling: if a free person explicitly accuses a muhsan (chaste, free, Muslim, adult) person of zina, and the accused demands punishment, the judge must administer eighty lashes to the accuser. The evidence is the Quranic verse 24:4, which commands flogging those who accuse chaste women (or men by analogy) without producing four witnesses. The requirement of four witnesses is implicit in the verse, as it is specific to zina. The demand (mutalaba) of the accused is a condition because qadhf involves a personal right (haqq al-‘abd) to clear one's honor. The accuser's freedom is also a condition for the full eighty lashes; for slaves, the number is halved (forty). Note: The Arabic phrase 'لِمَا تَلَوْنَا' refers to the preceding discussion about muhsan, which is defined by freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, and chastity from zina.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of adultery (zina) against a chaste person.
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (not previously convicted of zina).
مطالبة (mutalaba): The formal demand for punishment by the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Quranic basis for the hadd of qadhf?
A) Surah Al-Ma'idah, 5:38
B) Surah An-Nur, 24:4
C) Surah Al-Baqarah, 2:178
D) Surah Al-Isra, 17:32

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf is not automatically applied; it requires the victim's demand and a qualifying accusation.

The Drunkard's Confession and Apostasy: Pure Right of Allah vs. Human Rights
Distinguishing rulings based on the nature of the legal right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a drunkard's confession is rejected for hadd but accepted for qadhf, and state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of a drunkard's apostasy on marriage.

Core Idea
A drunkard's confession for a pure right of Allah is unreliable, but for human rights it is valid; apostasy requires conscious belief.

This lesson examines two distinct legal categories involving a drunkard (sakran). First, we explore why his confession for a hadd offense (like drinking) does not trigger punishment, while his confession for qadhf (false accusation) does. Second, we delve into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a drunkard utters words of apostasy, does his marriage dissolve? The source uses these cases to illustrate the Hanafi principle that pure rights of Allah are averted by doubt, whereas human rights are rigorously enforced.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish pure haqq Allah from human rights
Identify the legal nature of the hadd for drinking (khalis haqq Allah) versus the hadd for qadhf (involves haqq al-'abd). Why does this distinction matter for accepting the drunkard's confession?
2
Apply the rule of doubt (shubha)
Explain how the increased possibility of falsehood in the drunkard's confession creates a doubt that repels the hadd, per the maxim 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat'.
3
Compare the drunkard's capacity in different acts
Note that for transactions like divorce or manumission, the drunkard's utterances are effective. Why is confession for haqq Allah treated differently? Because confession is a proof that must be reliable, and intoxication undermines reliability in matters of pure divine right.
4
Analyze the apostasy dispute
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): apostasy requires belief, impossible during drunkenness, so marriage remains. Contrast with Zahir al-Riwayah: the utterance alone constitutes apostasy. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator prefers Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view, so the operative fatwa is that the marriage is not dissolved. Note the authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin (later preferred position).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ لَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَاتُ بِإِقْرَارِهِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ لِزِيَادَةِ اِحْتِمَالِ الْكِذْبِ فِي إِقْرَارِهِ فَيُحْتَالُ لِدَرْئِهِ لِأَنَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِ اللَّهِ. تَعَالَى بِخِلَافِ حَدِ الْقَذَفِ إِنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّ الْعَبْدِ وَ السَّكْرَانُ فِيهِ كَالصَّاحِى عُقُوبَةٌ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ تَصَرُّفَاتِهِ وَلَوِ ارْتَدَّ السَّكْرَانُ لَا تَبِينُ مِنْهُ امْرَأَتُهُ لأَنَّ الْكُفْرَ مِنْ بِابِ الْاعْتِقَادِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعَ السُّكْرِ وَهِذَا قَولُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَفِي ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ تَكُونُ رِدَّةٍ. [النص العربي مع الترجمة الأردية: نشہ کا اقرار کرنے والے پر حد جاری نہیں کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کے اس اقرار میں جھوٹ کا زیادہ احتمال رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر سے حد کو دور کرنے کے لئے صلہ معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ حد تو خالص حق الہی ہے۔ بخلاف جد قذف کے کیونکہ اس سے بندہ کا حق متعلق ہوتا ہے اور ایسے حقوق عبد میں وہ سب برابر ہوتے ہیں جو نشہ میں مست ہوں یا جو ہوش و حواس سب میں ہوں۔ تا کہ نشہ میں مست اپنی پوری سزا پائے۔ جیسے کہ اس کے دوسرے تصرفات اور معاملات طلاق واعتاق وغیرہ اس پر نافذ کر دیئے جاتے ہیں۔ لیکن اگر ایسا شخص یعنی نشہ میں مست مرتد ہو جائے تو اس کی بیوی اس سے مطلقہ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایک اعتقادی معاملہ ہے۔ اس لئے نشہ کے ساتھ اس کا متحقق نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ اور امام محمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا ہے لیکن ظاہر الروایۃ میں وہ مرتد ہو جائے گا۔ (لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کو چھوڑ کر قول اول ہی مختار ہے)۔]
And the drunk person is not subjected to hadd by his confession against himself due to the increased possibility of falsehood in his confession, so a stratagem is sought to repel it because it is the pure right of Allah Almighty, unlike the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because the right of the servant is involved in it; and the drunkard in it is like the sober one in terms of punishment upon him as in all his other actions. And if the drunkard apostatizes, his wife does not become separated from him because disbelief is from the realm of belief, and it cannot be realized with drunkenness. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) it is apostasy.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings concerning a drunkard (sakran). First, his voluntary confession regarding a hadd offense (like drinking alcohol) does not lead to the imposition of the fixed punishment (hadd). The reason is that his confession is unreliable due to the heightened possibility of falsehood caused by intoxication. Since the hadd is a pure right of Allah (haqq Allah), the law employs means (hila) to repel it, accepting the doubt in his confession. This contrasts with the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina), which involves the rights of the servant (haqq al-'abd); in such cases, the drunkard's confession is accepted like a sober person's, as seen in other legal transactions like divorce and manumission. Second, regarding apostasy: if a drunkard utters words of disbelief, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, his wife does not become divorced (talaq) because apostasy requires conscious belief, which is impossible during drunkenness. However, the well-known transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Imam Muhammad's six books states that he does become an apostate. The commentator prefers the first opinion (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), noting that it is the chosen (mukhtar) position for issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
السكران (al-sakran): A person who has consumed an intoxicant to the point of losing normal cognitive control, but not to the extent of total unconsciousness.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): A voluntary confession by a person against their own interest, in this context admitting to an act warranting hadd.
خالص حق الله (khalis haqq Allah): A legal right that belongs exclusively to Allah, where no individual's private right is involved, such as hadd for drinking.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The widely transmitted and authoritative version of the madhhab, recorded in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, why is a drunkard's confession for a hadd offense (like drinking) not accepted?
A) Because the drunkard is not legally responsible for any actions.
B) Because the hadd is a pure right of Allah, and the confession is unreliable due to increased chance of falsehood.
C) Because the hadd requires four witnesses and confession is insufficient.
D) Because the drunkard cannot be punished until he is sober.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a drunkard's confession is invalid for pure divine rights (hadd) but valid for human rights; and the preferred view is that his apostasy does not dissolve marriage because belief cannot coexist with intoxication.

Hadd for False Accusation (Qadf): Ruling, Conditions, and Execution
Ruling with proof, expansion on conditions and execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes for free, 40 for slave) and identify the five conditions of ihsan with their proofs, as well as explain the execution method.

Core Idea
A false accusation of zina against a chaste person incurs 80 lashes, but only if the victim demands it — the right to honor is personal.

This passage from the chapter on hudud establishes the fixed punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf). The ruling is based directly on the Quran (24:4). The text not only specifies the penalty but also details the conditions that must be met: the victim must be muhsan (chaste, free, sane, adult, Muslim) and must personally demand the hadd. Additionally, the passage explains how the punishment is carried out and how it differs for slaves. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying this hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its proof
Locate the central statement: 'If a man accuses a muhsan man or woman of zina... the judge imposes 80 lashes if the accuser is free.' Note the Quranic verse cited (24:4).
The imperative 'fajliduhum' establishes obligation; the number specifies the penalty.
2
Extract the conditions for the hadd to apply
List the conditions mentioned: the accuser must be free (or slave with 40 lashes), the accusation must be explicit (sarih al-zina), the victim must be muhsan, and the victim must demand the hadd.
The condition of the victim's demand is unique to qadhf because it involves a personal right.
3
Define 'muhsan' in Hanafi law
Identify the five components: free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste. Note the proofs for each: for freedom (Quran 4:25), for sanity/adulthood (disgrace not attaching to children/insane), for Islam (hadith), for chastity (no disgrace to a non-chaste person).
The term 'muhsan' is defined specifically for qadhf; it differs slightly from its meaning in zina.
4
Analyze the execution method
The lashes are distributed over the limbs (not concentrated), the offender is not stripped naked (unlike zina) because the cause is not certain, but thick clothing (fur, padding) is removed to ensure pain.
This reflects Hanafi's concern for proportionality and avoiding severity beyond necessity.
5
Apply the ruling to a slave accuser
Note the reduction to 40 lashes for a slave, based on the principle of half penalty (Quran 4:25 analogy).
This is consistent with other hudud where slaves receive half the free penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رُجَلًا مُحْصَنًا أَوِ امْرَأَةً مُحْصَنَةً بِصَرِيحِ الزِّنَا وَطَالَبَ الْمَقْذُوفُ بِالْحَدِّ حَدَّهُ الْحَاكِمُ ثَمَانِينَ سَوْطًا إِنْ كَانَ حُرًّا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ} إِلَى قَوْلِهِ {فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً} الْآيَةُ، وَالْمُرَادُ الرَّمْيُ بِالزِّنَا بِالْإِجْمَاعِ، وَفِي النَّصِّ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَيْهِ وَهُوَ اشْتِرَاطُ أَرْبَعَةٍ مِنَ الشُّهَدَاءِ إِذْ هُوَ مُخْتَصٌّ بِالزِّنَا. وَيُشْتَرَطُ مُطَالَبَةُ الْمَقْذُوفِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّهُ حَيْثُ دُفِعَ الْعَارُ. وَإِحْصَانُ الْمَقْذُوفِ لِمَا تَلَوْنَا. قَالَ: وَيُفَرَّقُ عَلَى أَعْضَائِهِ لِمَا مَرَّ فِي حَدِّ الزِّنَا، وَلَا يُجَرَّدُ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ لِأَنَّ سَبَبَهُ غَيْرُ مَقْطُوعٍ بِهِ فَلَا يُقَامُ عَلَى الشِّدَّةِ، بِخِلَافِ حَدِّ الزِّنَا. غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ يُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ وَالْحَشْوَةُ وَنَحْوُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَمْنَعُ إِبْصَالَ الْأَلَمِ بِهِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَاذِفُ عَبْدًا جُلِدَ أَرْبَعِينَ سَوْطًا لِمَكَانِ الرِّقِّ. وَالْإِحْصَانُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَقْذُوفُ حُرًّا عَاقِلًا بَالِغًا مُسْلِمًا عَفِيفًا عَنْ فِعْلِ الزِّنَا. أَمَّا الْحُرِّيَّةُ فَلِأَنَّهُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ الْإِحْصَانِ، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ} أَيِ الْحَرَائِرِ. وَالْعَقْلُ وَالْبُلُوغُ لِأَنَّ الْعَارَ لَا يَلْحَقُ الصَّبِيَّ وَالْمَجْنُونَ لِعَدَمِ تَحَقُّقِ فِعْلِ الزِّنَا مِنْهُمَا. وَالْإِسْلَامُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: «مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنٍ». وَالْعِفَّةُ لِأَنَّ غَيْرَ الْعَفِيفِ لَا يَلْحَقُهُ الْعَارُ، وَكَذَا الْقَاذِفُ صَادِقٌ فِيهِ.
And when a man accuses a muhsan man or a muhsan woman of explicit fornication, and the accused demands the hadd, the judge imposes eighty lashes if the accuser is free, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who accuse chaste women [of adultery]... then lash them with eighty lashes' (Quran 24:4). And the intended meaning by 'accusation' is accusation of fornication by consensus, and in the text there is an indication to it, which is the requirement of four witnesses, since that is specific to fornication. And the demand of the accused is required because it involves his right, since he is removing the disgrace. And the accused must be muhsan as we have recited. He said: And the lashes are distributed over his limbs as mentioned in the hadd of fornication, and he is not stripped of his clothes because its cause is not certain, so it is not implemented with severity, unlike the hadd of fornication. However, the fur coat and padding and the like that prevent the pain from reaching him are removed from him. And if the accuser is a slave, he is lashed forty stripes on account of slavery. And 'ihsan' is that the accused be free, sane, adult, Muslim, chaste from the act of fornication. As for freedom, because the name 'muhsan' is applied to the free: Allah Most High said: 'Then for them is half the punishment of muhsan women' (Quran 4:25), meaning free women. And sanity and adulthood because disgrace does not attach to a child or insane person due to the fact that the act of fornication is not realizable from them. And Islam because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' And chastity because the non-chaste person is not affected by disgrace, and likewise the accuser is truthful in it.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on hadd al-qadhf (punishment for false accusation of zina) lays out the core elements of the offense and its penalty. The ruling: if a free person explicitly accuses a muhsan (chaste, free, adult, sane Muslim) of zina, and the accused demands punishment, the judge must inflict 80 stripes. The primary evidence is the Qur'anic verse 24:4. The text notes that the requirement of four witnesses in the same verse indicates the offense is limited to zina. The accused's demand is a condition because the hadd involves his personal right to clear his honor. The definition of 'muhsan' for the victim is given: free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste (i.e., not previously convicted of zina). Then the method of execution: lashes are distributed over the body (not concentrated on one spot), and the accuser is not stripped naked because the cause (the accusation) is not absolutely certain (unlike zina where the act is proven). However, thick clothing like a fur coat (farw) and padded garments (hashwa) are removed to ensure the lashes cause pain. If the accuser is a slave, the penalty is 40 lashes, reduced because of his reduced status. The conditions of ihsan (freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, chastity) are explained with proofs: the verse about half the punishment for slave women indicates freedom is part of ihsan; sanity and adulthood are necessary because a child or insane person cannot actualize zina; a non-Muslim is not muhsan per the hadith; and a non-chaste person (one who has committed zina) is not harmed by the accusation, so no hadd applies.

Key Terms
القذف (al-qadhf): The act of falsely accusing an innocent, chaste person (muhsan) of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who is free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste (i.e., free from any past conviction or confession of zina).
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed, divinely ordained punishment for major offenses like zina, qadhf, theft, etc., which cannot be reduced or pardoned by the state once established.
العار (al-'ar): Disgrace or dishonor that attaches to a person due to an accusation of zina, which the hadd punishment serves to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadd is purely a right of Allah and does not involve the victim.
B) Because the victim has a personal right to have his honor cleared, and the hadd serves that right.
C) Because the judge cannot intervene without a formal complaint.
D) Because the accuser has the right to choose punishment.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for qadhf is 80 lashes for a free accuser and 40 for a slave, but only applies when the victim is muhsan and demands it, emphasizing the personal right to honor.

Administering Hadd al-Qadhf: Distribution and Stripping
Ruling on lashing procedure with analogy and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for lashing in hadd al-qadhf and explain why the convict is not stripped.

Core Idea
The cause of hadd al-qadhf is uncertain, so the punishment is carried out with less severity — no stripping.

The Hanafi school prescribes precise procedures for implementing hudud punishments. For hadd al-qadhf (lashing for false accusation of zina), the method of lashing is analogous to that of zina, but with a critical difference in the treatment of the convict's clothing. In this lesson, we examine the rationale behind this distinction, rooted in the certainty (or lack thereof) of the cause of the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage concerns the procedure for lashing in hadd al-qadhf. First, identify that the lashing itself is prescribed, and here the manner of execution is specified: distribution over limbs and non-stripping.
The hukm level is fard (obligatory) as part of the prescribed punishment.
2
Trace the analogy to zina
The author states that the lashes are to be distributed on the limbs 'as previously mentioned in the hadd of zina.' This indicates a direct analogy (qiyas) to the established method for zina.
The qiyas is khafi (hidden) because the commonality is not explicit but derived from the general nature of hadd.
3
Analyze the exception regarding stripping
Unlike zina, the convict is not stripped of his clothes. The reason given is that the cause (sabab) of qadhf is 'ghayr maqtu' bihi' (not certain). This uncertainty reduces the severity of the punishment.
Contrast with zina, where the cause is certain (e.g., confession or four witnesses), so severity is applied.
4
Identify the further refinement: thick clothing removal
While the convict is not stripped naked, thick garments like fur coats and padding are removed to ensure the lash reaches the body. This balances the principle of avoiding undue severity with the necessity of actual punishment.
This is an application of the legal maxim that a means that prevents the objective is removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ يُفَرَّقُ عَلَى أَعْضَائِهِ لِمَا مَرَّفِي حَدِ الزَّنَاءِ وَلَا يُجَرَّدُ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ لِاَنَّ سَبَبَهُ غَيْرُ مُقْطُوعٍ بِهِ فَلَايُقَامُ عَلَى الشَّدَّةِ بِخِلَافِ حَدَالِـزَنَاءِ غَيْرَانَهُ يُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْرُ وَالْحَشْوَلاتَ ذَالِكَ يَمْنَعُ إِبْصَالَ لا لَمِ بِهِ
ترجمہ اور تہمت لگانے والے کو اس کے مختلف اور متفرق اعضاء بدن پر درے لگائے جائیں گے جیسا کہ حد زنا میں گزر چکا ہے اور درے لگاتے وقت اس کے بدن کے کپڑے نہیں اتارے جائیں گے۔ کیونکہ حد قذف کا سبب یقینی اور قطعی نہیں ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ حدیفنی کے ساتھ قائم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ بخلاف حد زنا کے البتہ اس کے بدن سے اس کی پوستین اور لبادہ وغیرہ موٹے کپڑے اتار لئے بنائیں گے۔ کیونکہ اسے کپڑوں سے اس کو مار کی چوٹ نہیں پہنچے گی۔ تشريح ... قال و يفرق على اعضائه لمامر فى حد الزناء ولا يجرد من يثابه لان سببه ... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
He (the author) said: And the lashes will be distributed on his limbs as previously mentioned in the hadd of zina. And he will not be stripped of his clothes because its cause is not certain, so it is not carried out with severity, unlike the hadd of zina. However, his fur coat and padding are removed from him because that prevents the lash from reaching [his body]. Translation: And the accuser will be lashed on his various different body limbs as passed in the hadd of zina. And at the time of lashing, his body clothes will not be removed because the cause of hadd al-qadhf is not certain and definitive, therefore this hadd will not be carried out with severity. Contrary to the hadd of zina. However, his fur coat and cloak and thick clothes will be removed because the blow of the lash will not reach him through these clothes. Commentary: The meaning of the text is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the procedure for administering the lashing in hadd al-qadhf. It follows the same method as hadd al-zina: lashes are distributed over the limbs not concentrated on one spot. The convict is not stripped naked because the cause of qadhf (the accusation) is not certain (the accuser may be mistaken), so the punishment is carried out with less severity. However, thick clothing like a fur coat or padding is removed to ensure the lash reaches the body. This is contrasted with hadd al-zina where the cause is established by confession or proof, so severity is applied.

Key Terms
تجريد (tajrid): Stripping the convict of clothes before lashing.
سبب غير مقطوع به (sabab ghayr maqtu' bihi): A cause that is not certain; in qadhf, the accuser may be truthful but unable to prove.
فرّو (farw): Fur coat, a thick garment that must be removed.
حشوات (hashwāt): Padding or stuffed clothing that prevents the lash from reaching the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the cause of qadhf is not certain, so severity is avoided.
C) Because the accuser is often weak.
D) Because the punishment is only forty lashes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for hadd al-qadhf applies lashes like zina but avoids stripping due to the lesser certainty of the cause, balancing punishment with mercy.

Hadd al-Qadhf for a Slave and Definition of Ihsan
States the hadd for a slave qadhif and defines the conditions of ihsan for the accused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a slave qadhif receives 40 lashes, and list the five conditions of ihsan for the accused with their textual proofs.

Core Idea
A slave accuser gets 40 lashes; the accused's ihsan requires freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity.

In the law of qadhf (false accusation of zina), the punishment varies with the accuser's status, and the protection of the accused hinges on their being 'muhsan'. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies both: the hadd for a slave is half that of a free person, and ihsan consists of five specific conditions, each supported by clear textual evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a slave qadhif
The passage states that if the accuser is a slave, he receives forty lashes instead of eighty. Note the reason: due to slavery (al-riqq). This follows the general principle that a slave's hadd is half that of a free person.
The same half rule applies to other hudud punishments like zina for slaves.
2
Deconstruct the definition of ihsan
The word 'ihsan' is defined here as having five conditions: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity. These are conditions for the accused person to be considered 'muhsan' so that the accuser is liable for hadd. If any condition is missing, the accuser is not liable for the hadd of qadhf.
Contrast with Shafi'i: they also require marriage.
3
Trace the evidence for each condition
For freedom: Quran 4:25 uses 'muhsanat' to mean free women. For sanity and adulthood: a child or madman cannot commit zina, so no shame attaches. For Islam: hadith 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' (narrated by al-Hakim?). For chastity: an unchaste person is not harmed by the accusation.
The hadith on Islam is cited; check its authenticity later.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school includes marriage as a condition of ihsan, while the Hanafi school does not. The Hanafi position relies on the Quranic usage of 'muhsanat' for free women, not married ones.
The ikhtilaf has practical implications: a married adulterer would be considered muhsan by Shafi'is but not by Hanafis (since they require chastity, not marriage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام کی حد قذف
وَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَاذِفَ عَبْدَاجُلِدَ اَرْبَعِينَ سَوْطَالِمَكَانِ الرّقِ وَالْإِحْصَانُ اَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَقْدُوقَ حُرًّا عَاقِلًا بَالِغا مُسْلِمًا عَقِيمًا عَنْ فِعْلِ الزَّنَاءِ اَمَّا الْحُرِّيَّةُ فَلَانَّهُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ اِسْمُ الْإِحْصَانِ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ أَي الْحَرَائِرَ وَالْعَقْلُ وَ الْبُلُوعُ لِاَنَّ الْعَاوَلَا يَلْحَقَ بِالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ لِعَدْمِ تَحَقُّقِ فِعْلِ الزَّنَاءِ مِنْهُمَا وَالْإِسْلَامُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنِ وَالْعِفَّةُ لِاَنَّ غَيْرَ الْعَفِيْفِ لَا يَلْحَقُهُ الْعَارُّوَ كَذَا الْقَاذِقُ صَادِقٌ فِيهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر تہمت لگانے والا کوئی غلام ہو تو اس کی غلامی کی وجہ سے اسے چالیس درے لگائے جائیں گے۔ اس جگہ محصن ہونے کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ وہ آزاد، عاقل، بالغ ، مسلمان اور زنا کے کام سے پاک دامن ہو۔ اس میں آزادی کی قید اس لئے ہے کہ اس کو احصان کا نام دیا جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمان باری تعالے ہے فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنت من العذاب اس سے محصنات سے آزاد عورتیں مراد ہیں۔ اور عقل و بلوغ کی قید اس لئے ہے کہ نابالغ اور دیوانہ سے زنا کا وجود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کو عار بھی لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے اور اسلام کی قید اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے اللہ تعالے کے ساتھ شرک کیا وہ محسن نہیں ہے۔ (رواہ الحق) اور عفت (پاک دامن) کی قید اس لئے ہے کہ جو عفیف نہ ہو اس کو شرم لاحق نہیں ہوتی ہے اور تہمت لگانے والا بھی اپنی بات میں سچا ہو جاتا ہے۔ تشریح و ان كان القاذف عبد اجلد اربعين سوطالمكان الرق والاحصان ان يكون المقدوف .... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Hadd of Qadhf for a Slave: And if the accuser is a slave, he will be lashed forty lashes due to slavery. And Ihsan is that the accused be free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste (abstaining from the act of zina). As for freedom, because the name 'ihsan' is applied to it. Allah Most High said: 'So for them is half of what is for the muhsanat (free women) of punishment' meaning free women. And sanity and adulthood because shame does not attach to a child or a madman since the act of zina does not occur from them. And Islam because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' And chastity because shame does not attach to one who is not chaste, and the accuser would be truthful in it. Translation: And if the accuser is a slave, then due to his slavery, he will be lashed forty lashes. The meaning of muhsan here is that the accused is free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste from the act of zina. The condition of freedom is because he is given the name of ihsan. Thus, the command of Allah Most High: 'So for them is half of what is for the muhsanat of punishment' meaning free women. And the condition of sanity and adulthood is because a child or a madman does not feel shame due to the non-occurrence of the act of zina. And the condition of Islam is because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' (Narrated by al-Haq?) And the condition of chastity is because one who is not chaste does not feel shame, and the accuser would be truthful in his statement. Commentary: The meaning of the text is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) The hadd for a slave qadhif is forty lashes instead of eighty, due to slavery. (2) The definition of ihsan (chastity) for the accused, which requires five conditions: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and actual chastity (not having committed zina). Each condition is supported by evidence: freedom from the Quranic word 'muhsanat' meaning free women; sanity and adulthood because a child or madman cannot commit zina; Islam from a hadith that a mushrik is not muhsan; and chastity because an unchaste person is not harmed by the accusation. The Hanafi school uses these conditions to determine if the accused qualifies for the hadd.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being chaste; for qadhf, it requires freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity.
عبد (abd): A slave; in qadhf, a slave accuser receives half the lashes of a free person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ihsan in qadhf as a combination of freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity; a slave accuser receives 40 lashes.

Denying Lineage to Grandfather: No Hadd
Ruling on denying lineage to grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when someone denies a person's lineage to his grandfather and explain why no hadd is imposed.

Core Idea
Denying lineage to a grandfather is not qadhf because the statement is literally true — no hadd applies.

In the law of qadhf (false accusation of adultery), not every statement about lineage constitutes a punishable offense. This lesson examines a specific scenario: when someone says 'You are not the son of so-and-so' intending the grandfather. The Hanafi ruling is clear, and the reason is simple — truthfulness. We will explore the ruling and its basis, even as the full reasoning is cut off in our source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the Arabic: 'ولو قال لست بابن فلان يعني جده لم يحد'. The act is saying 'You are not the son of so-and-so', meaning the grandfather. The ruling is 'لم يحد' — he is not given the hadd punishment.
2
Understand the basis: truthful statement
The text gives the reason: 'لأنه صادق في كلامه' — because he is truthful in his speech. A person is indeed not the son of his grandfather; he is the son of his father. Thus, the statement is factually correct, so it cannot be a false accusation (qadhf).
Truth is a complete defense against wasm bi-ghayr al-zina (accusation of illegitimate birth).
3
Apply to similar cases
The text also mentions: 'ولو نسبه إلى جده لا يحد أيضًا' — if he attributes him to his grandfather, he also is not given the hadd. This is likely because attributing to the grandfather is not a denial of the father's paternity; it is still a true relation, albeit not the direct one. The reasoning is cut off but consistent with the principle of truthfulness.
Attributing someone to his grandfather is not a denial of his father's paternity and does not constitute qadhf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ لَسْتَ بِابْنِ فُلَانِ يَعْنِي جَدَّهُ لَمْ يُحَدُّ لِأَنَّهُ صَادِقَ فِي كَلَامِهِ وَ لَوْ نَسَبَهُ إِلَى جَدِهِ لَا يُحَدُّ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ
And if he said: 'You are not the son of so-and-so' meaning his grandfather, he will not be given the hadd because he is truthful in his speech. And if he attributed him to his grandfather, he will also not be given the hadd because...
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage begins a ruling that if someone says 'You are not the son of so-and-so' intending the grandfather, no hadd is imposed because the statement is factually true (one is not the son of one's grandfather). Similarly, if he attributes the person to his grandfather (i.e., says 'you are the son of your grandfather'), no hadd applies. The reasoning is cut off but likely because attributing to grandfather is not a denial of the actual father's paternity. This passage is incomplete; the full ruling with its proof would be on the next page.

Key Terms
جد (jadd): Grandfather (paternal).

Checkpoint

A) He is given hadd al-qadhf.
B) He is not given hadd because it is true.
C) He is given a ta'zir punishment.
D) He must prove his statement.

Key Takeaway
Denial of lineage to a grandfather does not trigger hadd because the statement is literally true; the false accusation must be against the actual father.

Conditions of Muhsan in Hadd al-Qadhf
Defining the five conditions with scriptural proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan for hadd al-qadhf and identify which proof establishes each condition.

Core Idea
For hadd al-qadhf to apply, the accused must be free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste — marriage is not required.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defines the legal concept of ihsan in the context of slander (qadhf). The text first provides scriptural evidence from the Quran and Sunnah to derive two conditions: freedom and Islam. It then adds the remaining conditions — adulthood, sanity, and chastity — to complete the definition. Understanding these conditions is essential because if any is missing, the accuser is not liable for the full hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Recognize that the passage concerns the punishment (hadd) for false accusation of adultery. The key question: when does the accuser become liable for 80 lashes?
This is a hudud ruling, requiring strict proof and conditions.
2
Analyze the Quranic dalil
The verse (4:25) states that slave women receive half the punishment of free muhsanat. This implies that freedom is a condition for being muhsan. Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the reduction is due to slavery, so the full punishment applies only to free persons.
The Quranic proof establishes freedom as a condition.
3
Analyze the hadith dalil
The hadith narrated by al-Hakim states that a polytheist is not muhsan. This directly establishes Islam as a condition. Note that this is a hadith ahad, but it is accepted in this context.
The hadith proves Islam is required.
4
Understand the consequence of missing conditions
The passage also mentions that if the accuser is a slave, his punishment is reduced to 40 lashes. This shows that the accuser's own status can affect the penalty. Additionally, if the accused lacks any condition, the hadd is not applied; instead, ta'zir may be used.
Missing conditions shift the punishment from hadd to ta'zir.
5
Synthesize the definition of ihsan
Combine the information: the five conditions are freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, and chastity. Note that marriage is not among them, distinguishing this from ihsan in zina.
Memorize the five conditions: free, adult, sane, Muslim, chaste.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنت من العذاب. روى الحاكم: من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن. وإن كان القاذف عبدا جلد أربعين سوطا لمكان الرق. والإحصان أن يكون المقدوف [؟] حرا عاقلا بالغا مسلما عفيفا.
For them is half of what is upon the muhsanat of punishment. Al-Hakim narrated: Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan. And if the accuser is a slave, he is lashed forty lashes due to slavery. And ihsan is that the accused be free, sane, adult, Muslim, chaste [؟].
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of ihsan (being muhsan) in the context of hadd al-qadhf (the punishment for false accusation of adultery). It begins with a Quranic verse (4:25) which states that slave women who commit adultery receive half the punishment of free muhsanat, proving that freedom is a condition for ihsan. Then it cites a hadith transmitted by al-Hakim: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan,' establishing that Islam is a condition. The matn then mentions that if the accuser is a slave, he is lashed 40 lashes instead of 80 due to slavery. Finally, the passage states the five conditions for the accused to be muhsan: free, sane, adult, Muslim, and chaste. These conditions must all be present for the hadd of 80 lashes to be wajib upon the accuser. The commentary follows the order of the matn, first providing the scriptural proofs, then the rule regarding a slave accuser, and finally the definition of ihsan.

Key Terms
احصان (ihsan): In the context of hadd al-qadhf, ihsan means that the accused possesses the five qualities: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Being free
B) Being adult and sane
C) Being married
D) Being Muslim and chaste

Key Takeaway
The five conditions for ihsan in hadd al-qadhf are freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and chastity — marriage is not required.

Hadd for Denial of Lineage (Nafy al-Nasab)
Stating the ruling of hadd for denying someone's lineage and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which denying a person's lineage incurs hadd according to the Hanafi school, and apply the ruling to different scenarios (father vs grandfather, anger context, mother's status).

Core Idea
Denial of lineage is punishable by hadd only when it implies qadhf of a free Muslim mother.

Denying someone's lineage (nafy al-nasab) is a serious accusation that can lead to the hadd punishment for qadhf. However, the Hanafi school specifies certain conditions that must be met. This lesson examines the ruling and its reasoning (ta'lil) as presented in al-Hidayah, covering three key scenarios: denial of the father, denial in anger versus without anger, and denial of the grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is denying another's paternal lineage by saying 'You are not your father's son.' The default ruling is that hadd is wajib on the speaker.
This is the basic case from which exceptions are derived.
2
Check the condition regarding the mother
The hadd applies only if the mother of the person addressed was a free Muslim woman at the time of his birth. The reason (illa) is that denying lineage implies accusing the mother of zina, which is qadhf.
If the mother is not free or Muslim, there is no hadd; ta'zir may apply instead.
3
Distinguish between anger and non-anger contexts
If the statement is made in anger, the literal insult is intended, so hadd applies. If made without anger, it is interpreted as a rebuke for lacking moral qualities, and no hadd is imposed.
The intent determined by context (anger vs calm) changes the ruling.
4
Examine the grandfather scenario
If the denial refers to a grandfather (e.g., 'You are not your grandfather's son'), no hadd applies. This is because the statement is literally true (a person is not the direct son of his grandfather) or is a metaphorical attribution.
The denial must specifically target the father to be considered qadhf.
5
Summarize the overall rule
Hadd for denial of lineage applies only when: (1) the denial is of the father, (2) the mother is free and Muslim, (3) the statement is made in anger.
Otherwise, no hadd; the matter may be dealt with via ta'zir or left entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ نَفَى نَسْبَ غَيْرِهِ وَقَالَ لَسْتَ لِأَبِيكَ فَإِنَّهُ يُحَدُّ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَتْ أُمُّهُ حُرَّةً مُسْلِمَةً لِأَنَّهُ فِي حَقِيقَةِ قَذْفٍ لِأُمِّهِ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ إِنَّمَا يُنْفَى عَنِ الزَّانِي لَا عَنْ غَيْرِهِ. وَمَنْ قَالَ لِغَيْرِهِ فِي غَضَبٍ لَسْتَ بِابْنِ فُلَانٍ لِأَبِيهِ الَّذِي يَدَّعِي لَهُ يُحَدُّ وَلَوْ قَالَ فِي غَيْرِ غَضَبٍ لَا يُحَدُّ لِأَنَّ عِنْدَ الْغَضَبِ يُرَادُ بِهِ حَقِيقَةُ سَبِّهِ وَفِي غَيْرِهِ يُرَادُ بِهِ الْمُعَاتَبَةُ بِسَفْيِ مُشَابَهَتِهِ آبَاهُ فِي أَسْبَابِ الْمُرُوءَةِ. وَلَوْ قَالَ لَسْتَ بِابْنِ فُلَانٍ يَعْنِي جَدَّهُ لَمْ يُحَدَّ لِأَنَّهُ صَادِقٌ فِي كَلَامِهِ وَلَوْ نَسَبَهُ إِلَى جَدِّهِ لَا يُحَدُّ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يُنْسَبُ إِلَيْهِ مَجَازًا.
And whoever denies the lineage of another and says, 'You are not your father's son,' then he is to be lashed with the hadd. This is when his mother was a free Muslim woman, because it is in reality a qadhf of his mother, since lineage is only denied from the fornicator, not from anyone else. And whoever says to another in anger, 'You are not the son of so-and-so,' meaning his father whom he claims, he is lashed. But if he says it without anger, he is not lashed, because in anger the literal meaning of insult is intended, whereas in other cases it is meant as a rebuke for his lack of resemblance to his father in qualities of manliness. And if he says, 'You are not the son of so-and-so,' meaning his grandfather, he is not lashed, because he is truthful in his speech. And if he attributes him to his grandfather, he is also not lashed, because he may be attributed to him metaphorically.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents three sub-rulings related to denial of lineage as a form of qadhf. First, outright denial of a person's paternal lineage (e.g., saying 'you are not your father's son') incurs hadd, but only if the mother of the person being addressed was a free Muslim woman. The reason ('illa) is that denying lineage necessarily implies accusing the mother of zina, because lineage is only denied from a fornicator. Second, if this statement is made in anger, hadd applies because it is intended as an insult; but if said without anger, it is interpreted as a gentle rebuke for lacking praiseworthy qualities, so no hadd. Third, if the denial refers to a grandfather (e.g., 'you are not your grandfather's son'), or if the person is attributed to his grandfather, no hadd applies because the statement may be true verbally or is a metaphorical attribution. The commentary follows the matn order, explaining each scenario and its rationale.

Key Terms
نفي النسب (nafy al-nasab): The act of denying that a person is the offspring of his claimed father, which is considered a form of qadhf (slander) if it implies zina of the mother.
قذف (qadhf): Slander: accusing a chaste person of illegal sexual intercourse without evidence. In this context, denial of lineage is considered qadhf of the mother.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes. Here, the hadd for qadhf is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does denying a person's lineage incur the hadd punishment according to the Hanafi school?
A) Always, regardless of the mother's status
B) Only if the mother is a free Muslim woman and the denial is of the father
C) Only if the denial is made in anger and the grandfather is mentioned
D) Only if the person is present

Key Takeaway
Denial of lineage incurs hadd only when the mother is free and Muslim, the denial is of the father, and it is made in anger.

Right to Demand Hadd for Accusing a Deceased Chaste Woman
Explaining who can demand hadd for qadhf of a deceased muhsana and disagreements among imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for who may demand hadd al-qadhf for a deceased muhsana, explain the basis of the dispute with the Shafi'i school, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreements of Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
The right to demand hadd for a deceased muhsana belongs only to those whose lineage is dishonored — the father and son — not to all heirs.

When a deceased chaste woman is accused of zina, the hadd punishment is still wajib on the accuser, but who can demand its enforcement? The Hanafi school restricts this right to the closest male relatives whose lineage is directly impugned, while the Shafi'i school extends it to all heirs. Moreover, within the Hanafi school, there are disagreements among the imams about the scope of this right — whether it reaches grandsons through daughters, whether it exists when the direct son is alive, and whether a kafir or slave son can claim. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and these internal differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific claim: only the father and son (and their male-line descendants) of the deceased may demand hadd for qadhf. Explain the underlying 'illah: dishonor attaches to them because of their partitive relationship (جزئية) with the deceased.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all heirs can demand hadd, because in his school the right to hadd is inheritable property.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that just as other rights (e.g., monetary compensation) pass to heirs, so does the right to demand hadd. The hadd is a right of the victim that transfers to the estate.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the right is not inherited; it arises from direct harm to lineage. Proof: even a murderer who is barred from inheritance can still demand hadd for his deceased relative, showing it is not based on inheritance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and intra-Hanafi details
The practical difference: under Hanafi, only father/son (and descendants) can bring the case; under Shafi'i, any heir can. Also, within Hanafi, the right extends to grandsons (even through daughters) and to kafir/slave sons, contrary to the views of Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar.
The mufta bihi position is the broader view as presented in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ لَهُ يَا ابْنَ الزَّانِيَةِ وَأُمُّهُ مَيْتَةٌ مُحْصَنَةٌ فَطَالَبَ الْإِبْنُ بِحَدِّهِ حُدَّ الْقَاذِفُ لِأَنَّهُ قَذَفَ مُحْصَنَةً بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَلَا يُطَالَبُ بِحَدِّ الْقَذْفِ لِلْمَيِّتِ إِلَّا مَنْ يَقَعُ الْقَدْحُ فِي نَسَبِهِ بِقَذْفِهِ وَهُوَ الْوَالِدُ وَالْوَلَدُ لِأَنَّ الْعَارَ يَلْتَحِقُ بِهِ لِمَكَانِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ فَيَكُونُ الْقَذْفُ مُتَنَاوِلًا لَهُ مَعْنًى وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ يَثْبُتُ حَقُّ الْمُطَالَبَةِ لِكُلِّ وَارِثٍ لِأَنَّ حَدَّ الْقَذْفِ يُورَثُ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى مَا نُبَيِّنُ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يَثْبُتُ الْمُطَالَبَةُ بِطَرِيقِ الْإِرْثِ بَلْ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلِهَذَا يَثْبُتُ عِنْدَنَا لِلْمَحْرُومِ عَنِ الْمِيرَاثِ بِالْقَتْلِ وَيَثْبُتُ لِوَلَدِ الْبِنْتِ كَمَا يَثْبُتُ لِوَلَدِ الْإِبْنِ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٍ وَيَثْبُتُ لِوَلَدِ الْوَلَدِ حَالَ قِيَامِ الْوَلَدِ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ. وَإِذَا كَانَ الْمَقْذُوفُ مُحْصَنًا جَازَ لِابْنِهِ الْكَافِرِ وَالْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ بِالْحَدِّ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ وَهُوَ يَقُولُ الْقَذْفُ يَتَنَاوَلُهُ [؟]
And if he says to him, 'O son of the adulteress,' while his mother was a deceased muhsana, and the son demands his hadd, the accuser is lashed, because he accused a muhsana after her death. And the hadd of qadhf for a deceased person cannot be demanded except by the one whose lineage is impugned by this qadhf, namely the father and the son, because the dishonor attaches to him due to the partial (partitive) relationship, so the qadhf encompasses him in meaning. According to al-Shafi'i, the right to demand is established for every heir, because in his view the hadd of qadhf is inheritable, as we will explain. According to us, the demand is not established through inheritance but for the reason we mentioned; thus, according to us, it is established for the one deprived of inheritance due to killing, and it is established for the son of a daughter just as it is for the son of a son, contrary to Muhammad. And it is established for the son of a son when the son is present, contrary to Zufar. And if the accused is muhsan, it is permissible for his son, even if he is a disbeliever or a slave, to demand the hadd, contrary to Zufar, who says that the qadhf encompasses him [؟].
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario of accusing a deceased chaste woman (muhsana) of zina. The qadhf is valid and the accuser is lashed because the woman was muhsana at the time of her death. Only those who suffer dishonor due to the accusation can demand the hadd: the deceased's father and son (and by extension, grandfather and grandson through the male line), because the dishonor attaches to them due to their partitive connection (جزئية). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all heirs can demand the hadd because in his school, the right to hadd is inheritable like property. The Hanafi position is that it is not inherited but based on direct harm. This is proven by the fact that even a person who is barred from inheritance (e.g., a murderer) can demand hadd according to Hanafis. Moreover, the right extends to the son of a daughter (grandson), contrary to Imam Muhammad, and to a grandson even if the son is alive, contrary to Imam Zufar. Additionally, if the accused is muhsan, his son—even if a disbeliever or a slave—can demand the hadd, while Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that the accusation does not encompass such a son (perhaps because the dishonor is not felt).

Key Terms
مطالبة بالحد (mutalaba bil-hadd): The legal right to demand the execution of the prescribed punishment (hadd) against a guilty person, specifically in the context of qadhf.
محصنة (muhsana): A chaste, free, adult Muslim woman who has been married (or has had lawful sexual relations) and is protected from false accusations.
جزئية (juz'iyya): Partitive relationship; the idea that the father and son are 'parts' of each other in lineage, so dishonor to one affects the other.
محروم عن الميراث بالقتل (mahrum 'an al-mirath bil-qatl): A person who is barred from inheritance because they caused the death of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who can demand hadd al-qadhf when the accused is a deceased muhsana?
A) Any heir, regardless of relationship
B) Only the son or father of the deceased
C) Only the husband of the deceased
D) Only the ruler (sultan)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the right to demand hadd for qadhf of a deceased muhsana belongs exclusively to the father and son (and their male-line descendants) based on direct dishonor to their lineage, and this right extends even to grandsons, kafirs, and slaves, contrary to Shafi'i and some Hanafi imams.

No Hadd for Saying 'You Are Not the Son of Your Grandfather'
Ruling on attributing to grandfather in slander cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two slander scenarios involving paternal attribution and explain why no hadd applies.

Core Idea
Truthful statements and metaphorical attributions do not trigger the hadd for qadhf.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani explains two cases where a statement about someone's lineage does not constitute slander punishable by hadd. The key insight is that for the hadd of qadhf to apply, the statement must be a clear and false imputation of illegitimate birth. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the boundary between offensive speech and legally punishable slander.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage carefully. There are two distinct statements considered: (1) 'You are not the son of your grandfather' and (2) 'You are the son of your grandfather'. Note that both are ruled to have no hadd.
The first scenario is a negation, the second a positive attribution.
2
Determine the basis for no hadd in the first scenario
Analyze why 'You are not the son of your grandfather' incurs no hadd. The passage states the speaker is truthful (sadiq). This is factually correct: a person is not the son of his grandfather but his son. Truthfulness is a complete defense against qadhf.
Qadhf requires a false accusation of zina.
3
Determine the basis for no hadd in the second scenario
Analyze why 'You are the son of your grandfather' incurs no hadd. The passage explains it is a metaphorical attribution (majaz). In common Arabic usage, calling someone 'son of his grandfather' is a figurative expression for lineage, not a literal claim of paternity. Since it is not an imputation of illegitimacy, hadd is not applied.
Concept of majaz is key here.
4
Extract the underlying principle
From both scenarios, deduce the principle: For hadd to apply, the statement must be a clear, false, and direct accusation of illegitimate birth. Truthfulness and metaphorical speech fall outside this scope.
This principle protects speech that is not clearly slanderous.
5
Apply the principle to similar scenarios
Consider other statements like 'You are not the son of your uncle' or 'You are the son of your tribe'. Determine that these are also either truthful or metaphorical, hence no hadd.
Not every insult about lineage carries hadd.

Source Text

باب حد القذف قَدْيُنسَبُ إِلَيْهِ مَجَازًا
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم
ترجمہ اور اگر یوں کہا کہ تم فلاں یعنی اپنے دادا کے بیٹا نہیں ہو تو اسے حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی کیونکہ وہ تو اپنے کہنے میں سچا ہے اور اگر یہ کہا کہ تم اپنے دادا کے بیٹے ہو تو بھی حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی کیونکہ بھی دادا کی طرف مجاز انسبت کر دیتے ہیں۔ تشریح... و لو قال لست بابن فلان یعنی جده لم يحد لانه صادق في كلامه و لو نسبه ..... .. الخ
Chapter of Hadd for Slander. It is metaphorically attributed to him. Translation: And if he said, 'You are not the son of so-and-so,' meaning his grandfather, he will not be subject to hadd, because he is truthful in his statement. And if he said, 'You are the son of your grandfather,' he will also not be subject to hadd, because he attributively relates him to his grandfather metaphorically. Commentary... 'And if he said, 'You are not the son of so-and-so,' meaning his grandfather, he will not be subject to hadd because he is truthful in his statement, and if he attributed him [to his grandfather]... etc.'
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah regarding slander (qadhf) when the insult involves attributing someone to their grandfather. The author explains two scenarios: (1) If someone says 'You are not the son of your grandfather,' no hadd is applied because the statement is literally true—the addressee is indeed not the son of his grandfather but his son. (2) If someone says 'You are the son of your grandfather,' no hadd is applied either, because here 'son of grandfather' is understood metaphorically, as a common expression for lineage, not as an accusation of illegitimacy. The key principle is that for hadd to apply, the statement must clearly impute illegitimate birth. Since these statements either are truthful or carry a permissible metaphorical meaning, they fall outside the scope of slander punishment.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of adultery or fornication punishable by hadd.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage; here, calling someone 'son of grandfather' is a permissible metaphorical attribution, not literal.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes, here specifically for false accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no hadd for saying 'You are the son of your grandfather'?
A) Because the statement is true and the addressee is indeed the son of his grandfather
B) Because the statement is a metaphorical attribution, not an imputation of illegitimate birth
C) Because the grandfather is not alive
D) Because the accuser is a close relative

Key Takeaway
Truthful statements and metaphorical expressions do not constitute slander (qadhf) and thus do not incur the hadd punishment.

Right to Demand Hadd for Slander of a Deceased Muhsan: Hanafi vs Shafi'i and Intra-Hanafi Details
Ruling on slander of deceased muhsan and who demands hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slander of a deceased muhsan woman, identify who can demand hadd, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Imam al-Shafi'i and from intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Only the parent or child of a deceased muhsan can demand hadd — the shame attaches to them by part-whole relationship.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah examines a specific case of qadhf: a man slanders another by calling him 'son of an adulteress' after his mother's death, while she was muhsan. The text rules that the slanderer receives hadd, but restricts the right to demand punishment to those whose lineage is directly harmed. It then contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows all heirs to demand, and presents internal Hanafi disagreements about descendants through daughters and grandchildren.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first part: the slanderer said 'O son of an adulteress' to a man whose mother was deceased and muhsan. The son demands hadd. The ruling is that the slanderer is punished with hadd.
The hadd is established because the slandered person (the mother) was muhsan.
2
Determine who can demand hadd according to Hanafis
The text states that only those whose lineage is affected by the slander can demand: the father or child of the deceased, due to the part-whole relationship (juz'iyya). The shame attaches to them.
This is based on the principle of direct harm, not inheritance.
3
Contrast the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that every heir can demand, because he considers the right to demand hadd for qadhf to be inheritable.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the demand is not by inheritance but because the slander directly harms the child/parent. Therefore, even a person excluded from inheritance (like a murderer) can demand hadd.
This shows the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Note the intra-Hanafi extensions
The text also notes that the child of a daughter can demand (contrary to Muhammad), and the grandchild can demand even when the parent is alive (contrary to Zufar).
These are extensions based on the same principle of part-whole.

ترجمہ اور اگر کسی مرد سے کہا اے زانیہ کے بیٹے حالانکہ اس کی محصنہ ماں مرچکی ہے اس پر بیٹے نے اس کے خلاف قذف کا دعوی کیا تو قاذف کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایک محصنہ عورت کو اس کے مرنے کے بعد زناکاری کی تہمت لگائی ہے۔ ف۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وہ عورت زندہ ہوتی اور تہمت کے بعد مرجاتی وہ حد ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ العنایہ اور مردہ کے واسطے حد قذف کا مطالبہ کوئی بھی نہیں کرسکتا ہے سوائے اس شخص کے جس کے نسب میں اس مردہ کے قذف سے عیب و عار لاحق ہوا ہو اور وہ اس مردہ کا باپ یا بیٹا ہی ہو سکتا ہے۔ یعنی نسب میں اوپر کی جانب باپ اور داد و غیرہ ہو یا نیچے کی جانب بیٹا اور پوتا اور ان کی اولاد ہو نیچے تک ہو۔ کیونکہ والد یا نیچے کی اولاد کو مردہ سے جزئیت کی وجہ سے اس قذف سے عار اور شرمندگی ہوگی۔ اس بناء پر بظاہر صرف مردہ پر قذف کرنا حقیقت میں ان تمام کو قذف کرنا اور عار دلانا ہو گا اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس مطالبہ کا حق اس کے تمام وارثوں کو ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک حد قذف بھی ایک میراث ہوتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم آئندہ اسے بیان کریں گے اور ہمارے نزدیک مطالبہ کرنے کا حق میراث کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بلکہ اس وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اس کا الزام و قذف میں یہ لوگ بھی شریک ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے جو شخص میراث سے محروم ہو مثلاً اس نے مردہ کو تل کر دیا ہو اس کو بھی ہمارے نزدیک حد قذف کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ جس طرح بیٹے کی اولاد کا مطالبہ کر سکتی ہے۔ اس طرح یٹی کی اولاد بھی حد قذف لگانے کا مطالبہ کرسکتی ہے اس مسئلہ میں امام محمدرحمہ اللہ علیہ ا اختلاف ہے اور اگرلڑ کا موجودہ ہو تو بھی اس کی موجودگی میں اس لڑکے کی اولاد کو اپنے مردہ دار لیا نانا کے قذف کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوتا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں امام زفر رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا اختلاف ہے۔
And if he said to him, 'O son of an adulteress,' while his mother is dead and was muhsan, and the son demanded his hadd, the slanderer is punished with hadd, because he slandered a muhsan woman after her death. And no one can demand hadd for the deceased except one whose lineage is affected by the slander, and that is the father and the child, because the shame attaches to him due to the part-whole relationship, so the slander includes him in meaning. According to al-Shafi'i, the right of demand is established for every heir, because the hadd for slander is inheritable in his view, as we will explain. According to us, the demand is not by way of inheritance, but for what we mentioned. Therefore, with us, it is established for one who is deprived of inheritance by killing, and it is established for the child of a daughter just as it is established for the child of a son, contrary to Muhammad. And it is established for the child of the child while the child is alive, contrary to Zufar. [Urdu translation]
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses the situation where a man says to another, 'O son of an adulteress,' after the addressee's mother has died and she was a chaste (muhsan) woman. The ruling is that the slanderer is subject to hadd, because he falsely accused a muhsan woman even after her death. However, the right to demand hadd for a deceased person is restricted to those whose lineage is damaged by the slander—namely, the deceased's father or child (and by extension, grandfather or grandson). This is because the shame of the accusation attaches to them through the part-whole relationship (juz'iyya). The text then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that every heir can demand the hadd because he considers hadd for qadhf to be inheritable. The Hanafi response is that the right to demand is not based on inheritance but on the direct harm to one's lineage. Consequently, even a person who is excluded from inheritance (e.g., due to killing the deceased) can demand hadd. Additionally, the right extends to the children of daughters (grandchildren) just as it does to sons' children, contrary to Imam Muhammad. It also extends to grandchildren even when the parent is alive, contrary to Imam Zufar. The commentary emphasizes that these rulings are based on the principle that the slander meaningfully includes the child or parent in its harm.

Key Terms
محصن (muḥṣan): A person (male or female) who is free, adult, Muslim, and has consummated a valid marriage; slandering such a person invites hadd.
عار (ʿār): Shame or disgrace that attaches to the family lineage due to the slander.
جزئية (juzʾiyya): Part-whole relationship; e.g., a child is a part of the parent, so shame on the parent affects the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, who can demand hadd for slander of a deceased muhsan woman?
A) All her heirs
B) Only her husband
C) Only her father and son (and their descendants)
D) Only her brother

Key Takeaway
The right to demand hadd for slander of a deceased muhsan is based on direct lineage harm, not inheritance, so only parents and children (and their descendants) can demand in the Hanafi school.

intermediate
