Son of Slandered Muhsan Can Demand Hadd
Ruling on son of muhsan demanding hadd with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a son can demand hadd for slander of his muhsan father even if the son is a kafir or slave, and explain the Hanafi response to Imam Zufar's objection.

Core Idea
The son of a muhsan may demand hadd even if he is a kafir or slave.

This lesson explores a subtle issue in qadhf: when the slandered person (maqdūf) is muhsan, his son can demand the hadd penalty. The Hanafi school affirms this right even if the son is a disbeliever or a slave, contrary to Imam Zufar's view. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequences of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The ruling: son of a muhsan slandered person may demand hadd. Condition: the slandered person must be muhsan.
The son's status (kafir, slave) does not bar him.
2
Internal Hanafi dispute (Imam Zufar)
Imam Zufar held that the son cannot demand because the slander is directed at the father, not the son; the son's right would be via inheritance, which is not accepted.
Zufar also argued that the shame does not fully transfer.
3
Hanafi response
The complete ta'r (reproach) of slandering a muhsan extends to his son; disbelief or slavery does not affect eligibility to demand hadd.
Key principle: kufr does not nullify ahliyyat al-istihqaq.
4
Thamarah al-Khilaf
Under Zufar's view, a kafir or slave son cannot demand; under the majority Hanafi view, they can. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
Practical difference in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَ الْمَقْدُوتُ مُحْصَنًا جَازَ لِابْنِهِ الْكَافِرِ وَ الْعَبْدِانْ يُطَالِبَ بِالْحَدِ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ هُوَ يَقُولُ الْقَذْفُ يَتَنَاوَلُهُ مَعْنَى لِوُجُوعِ الْعَارِإِلَيْهِ وَ لَيْسَ طَرِيقُهُ الْإِرْتَ عِنْدَنَا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا كَانَ مُتَنَاوِلَالَهُ صُورَةٌ وَمَعْنِّى وَلَنَا إِنَّهُ عَيَّرَهُ بِقَدْفِ مُحْصَنٍ فَيَأْخُذُهُ بِالْحَدِوَهَذَا لِاَنَّ الْإِحْصَانَ فِي الَّذِي يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الزِّنَاءِ شَرْطٌ لِيَقَعَ تَعْسِيرًا عَلَى الْكَمَالِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ هَذَا التَّعْبِيرُ الْكَامِلُ إِلَى وَلَدِهِ وَالْكُفْرُ لَاتِنَا فِي اَهْلِيَّةَ الْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا تَنَاوَلَهُ الْقَذْقُ نَفْسَهُ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوْجَدِ التَّعْيِيرُ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ لِفَقْدِ الْإِحْصَانِ فِي الْمَنْسُوبِ إِلَى الزِّنَاءِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی گئی اگر وہ محسن ہو تو اس کے بیٹے کو حد کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اگر چہ وہ بیٹا کا فر یا کسی دوسرے کا غلام ہو اس میں امام زفر رحمتہ اللہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ کہتے ہیں کہ معنی کے اعتبار سے یہ تہمت اس کے بیٹے کو بھی شامل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس تہمت سے خود اس لڑکے سے بھی الحاق عاز ہوا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ بات میراث کے طور پر نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا یہ تہمت ظاہری و باطنی طور پر اسے شامل ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تہمت لگانے والے نے جسے تہمت لگائی گئی ہے اس کے بیٹے کو اس طرح عار دلائی کہ اس کے مصن باپ کو تہمت لگائی ہے اس لئے بیٹا حد قذف جاری کرنے کے لئے اس کے قازف کو پکڑے گا۔ کیونکہ جس شخص کو زنا کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے اس کا محصن ہونا شرط ہے۔ تاکہ پورے طور پر یہ کہا جاسکے کہ اس نے عار دلائی اور شرمندہ کیا ہے۔ پھر اس کی شرمندگی اور رسوائی اس کے بیٹے کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گی اور لڑ کا حد لگوانے کا مطالبہ کر سکے گا اور ایسے استحقاق میں کافر ہونے سے اس کی لیاقت ختم نہیں ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر خود اس کا فریا غلام کو قذف کیا گیا تو وہ اپنا مطالبہ نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں پورے طور پر عار دلانا نہیں پایا جاتا ہے۔ اگر زنا کی طرف اس کی نسبت کی گئی ہو۔
تشريح و اذا كان المقذوف محضا جاز لابنه الكافر و العبدان يطالب بالحد خلافا لزفر هو يقول الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
غلام کی آزاد ماں پر آقا نے زنا کی تہمت لگائی یا اپنے بیٹے کی آزاد مسلمان ماں پر تہمت لگائی تو غلام اور بیٹے کو حد کے مطالبہ کا حق ہے یا نہیں
وَلَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِانْ يُطَالِبَ مَوْلَاهُ بِقَدْفِ أُمِّهِ الْحُرَّةِ وَلَا لِلابْنِ أَنْ يُطَالَبَ آبَاهُ بِقَذْفِ أُمِّهِ الْحُرَّةِ الْمُسْلِمَةِ لِآن الْمَوْلَى لَا يُعَاقَبُ بِسَبِبٍ عَبْدِهِ وَكَذَا الْآبُ بِسَبَبِ ابْنِهِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقَادُ الْوَالِد وَلَا السَّيِّدُ بِعَبْدِهِ وَلَوْ كَانَ لَهَا ابْنٌ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ لَهُ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ لِتَحَقُّقِ السَّبَبِ وَالْعِدَامِ الْمَانِعِ
ترجمہ اگر غلام کے مولیٰ نے غلام کی آزاد ماں کو قذف کیا یا اپنے بیٹے کی آزاد مسلماں ماں کو قذف کیا تو غلام یا بیٹے کو حد قذف کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے کیونکہ مولیٰ کو اس کے اپنے غلام کی وجہ سے سزا نہیں دی جاسکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح باپ کو بھی اس کے بیٹے کی وجہ سے عذاب نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسی بناء پر بیٹے کو قتل کر دینے کی بناء پر قصاص میں قتل نہیں کیا جاتا ہے اور غلام کو قتل کر دینے سے بھی اس کے مولی کو قتل نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر اس عورت کا کوئی لڑکا دوسرے شوہر سے ہو تو اس کو مطالبہ کا اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ سبب یعنی قذف موجود ہے اور اس میں رکاوٹ ڈالنے والی کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ ف۔ لیکن یہ حکم دنیا وی ہے اور اگر جھوٹی تہمت لگائی پھر تو بہ کے بغیر مر گیا تو آخرت میں عذاب ہوگا جیسا کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث میں ہے جس نے اپنے غلام کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی تو قیامت کے دن اس پر حد قائم کی جائے گی۔ البتہ اس صورت میں جب کہ مولیٰ نے جیسا کہا ویا ہی ہو۔ (رواہ البخاری و مسلم)
And if the slandered person is muhsan, it is permissible for his son, even if he is a disbeliever or a slave, to demand the hadd, contrary to Zufar. He says: The slander includes him in meaning because the shame reverts to him, and its way is not inheritance according to us, so it becomes as if it included him in form and meaning. Our proof: indeed, he slandered a muhsan, so he takes him with the hadd. This is because muhsan in the one attributed to zina is a condition for the complete ta'zir (reproach). Then this complete reproach returns to his child, and disbelief does not harm the eligibility of right. Contrary to if the slander includes him directly (i.e., if the son himself is slandered), because the complete reproach is not found due to the lack of muhsan in the one attributed to zina. [Urdu translation] ... And it is not for the slave to demand his master for slander of his free mother, nor for the son to demand his father for slander of his free Muslim mother, because the master is not punished due to his slave, and likewise the father due to his son. For this reason, the parent is not subject to qisas for killing his child, nor the master for killing his slave. But if she has a son from another [husband], he has the right to demand, because the cause (slander) is present and there is no preventing factor. [Urdu translation and hadith]
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This section covers two separate rulings related to demanding hadd for qadhf. First ruling: When the person being slandered (e.g., called 'son of an adulteress') is himself a muhsan, his son can demand hadd even if the son is a disbeliever or a slave. This is the Hanafi position, with Imam Zufar dissenting. Zufar argues that the slander includes the son in meaning, but that would require the son to be the direct target. The Hanafi response is that the complete shame (of calling a muhsan an adulterer) extends to his son, and disbelief does not affect the capacity to demand hadd. If the slander directly targets a non-muhsan person, the son cannot demand because there is no complete shame. Second ruling: A slave cannot demand hadd against his master for slandering the slave's free mother, and a son cannot demand hadd against his father for slandering the son's free Muslim mother. This is because the master and father are not punished through their subordinates/children. Analogous rules in qisas are cited. However, if the woman has a son from another husband, that son can demand because there is no preventing relationship. The passage ends with a hadith warning of punishment in the Hereafter for such false accusations.

Key Terms
مقذوف (maqdūf): The person who is slandered; the target of the qadhf.
اهلية الاستحقاق (ahliyyat al-istihqāq): Capacity to claim a right; here, disbelief does not negate it for demanding hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a slave son demand hadd for slander of his muhsan father?
A) Yes, because the shame extends to him.
B) No, because a slave lacks legal capacity.
C) Only if the father is also a slave.
D) No, because slavery prevents inheritance.

Key Takeaway
The son of a muhsan maqdūf may demand hadd regardless of his own status (slave or kafir) because the complete shame reverts to him.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Prohibition of Demanding Hadd Against Father/Master
Ruling on prohibition of demanding hadd against father or master.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a slave cannot demand hadd against his master for slandering his free mother, and a son cannot demand against his father for slandering his free Muslim mother, and explain the legal rationale based on the principle that a superior is not punished through his subordinate.

Core Idea
A slave cannot demand hadd against his master, nor a son against his father, for slander of the mother.

This lesson examines a specific limitation in the law of qadhf: a slave cannot demand hadd against his master for slandering the slave's free mother, and a son cannot demand against his father for slandering the son's free Muslim mother. The rationale is that a master or father is not punished due to their subordinate (slave or child). This principle is also reflected in qisas rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited claims
Two cases: slave vs master for slander of slave's free mother; son vs father for slander of son's free Muslim mother.
The mother must be free and, in the son's case, Muslim.
2
State the ruling
The slave and son cannot demand hadd in these cases. The hadd is not applicable against the master or father.
This is a prohibition on the claim, not a negation of the slander itself.
3
Understand the rationale
The master is not punished because of his slave's cause; similarly, the father is not punished because of his son's cause. This is analogous to qisas: a parent is not executed for killing his child, nor a master for killing his slave.
The rationale is based on hierarchical relationships and legal capacity.
4
Recognize the exception
If the mother has a son from another husband (not the slanderer), that son can demand hadd because there is no preventing relationship.
The preventing factor is the direct master-slave or father-son relationship between the slanderer and the claimant.

ترجمہ اور جس شخص کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی گئی اگر وہ محسن ہو تو اس کے بیٹے کو حد کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اگر چہ وہ بیٹا کا فر یا کسی دوسرے کا غلام ہو اس میں امام زفر رحمتہ اللہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ کہتے ہیں کہ معنی کے اعتبار سے یہ تہمت اس کے بیٹے کو بھی شامل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس تہمت سے خود اس لڑکے سے بھی الحاق عاز ہوا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ بات میراث کے طور پر نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا یہ تہمت ظاہری و باطنی طور پر اسے شامل ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تہمت لگانے والے نے جسے تہمت لگائی گئی ہے اس کے بیٹے کو اس طرح عار دلائی کہ اس کے مصن باپ کو تہمت لگائی ہے اس لئے بیٹا حد قذف جاری کرنے کے لئے اس کے قازف کو پکڑے گا۔ کیونکہ جس شخص کو زنا کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے اس کا محصن ہونا شرط ہے۔ تاکہ پورے طور پر یہ کہا جاسکے کہ اس نے عار دلائی اور شرمندہ کیا ہے۔ پھر اس کی شرمندگی اور رسوائی اس کے بیٹے کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گی اور لڑ کا حد لگوانے کا مطالبہ کر سکے گا اور ایسے استحقاق میں کافر ہونے سے اس کی لیاقت ختم نہیں ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر خود اس کا فریا غلام کو قذف کیا گیا تو وہ اپنا مطالبہ نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں پورے طور پر عار دلانا نہیں پایا جاتا ہے۔ اگر زنا کی طرف اس کی نسبت کی گئی ہو۔
تشريح و اذا كان المقذوف محضا جاز لابنه الكافر و العبدان يطالب بالحد خلافا لزفر هو يقول الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔

ترجمہ اگر غلام کے مولیٰ نے غلام کی آزاد ماں کو قذف کیا یا اپنے بیٹے کی آزاد مسلماں ماں کو قذف کیا تو غلام یا بیٹے کو حد قذف کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے کیونکہ مولیٰ کو اس کے اپنے غلام کی وجہ سے سزا نہیں دی جاسکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح باپ کو بھی اس کے بیٹے کی وجہ سے عذاب نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسی بناء پر بیٹے کو قتل کر دینے کی بناء پر قصاص میں قتل نہیں کیا جاتا ہے اور غلام کو قتل کر دینے سے بھی اس کے مولی کو قتل نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر اس عورت کا کوئی لڑکا دوسرے شوہر سے ہو تو اس کو مطالبہ کا اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ سبب یعنی قذف موجود ہے اور اس میں رکاوٹ ڈالنے والی کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ ف۔ لیکن یہ حکم دنیا وی ہے اور اگر جھوٹی تہمت لگائی پھر تو بہ کے بغیر مر گیا تو آخرت میں عذاب ہوگا جیسا کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث میں ہے جس نے اپنے غلام کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی تو قیامت کے دن اس پر حد قائم کی جائے گی۔ البتہ اس صورت میں جب کہ مولیٰ نے جیسا کہا ویا ہی ہو۔ (رواہ البخاری و مسلم)

Commentary
This section covers two separate rulings related to demanding hadd for qadhf. First ruling: When the person being slandered (e.g., called 'son of an adulteress') is himself a muhsan, his son can demand hadd even if the son is a disbeliever or a slave. The Hanafi response is that the complete shame (of calling a muhsan an adulterer) extends to his son, and disbelief does not affect the capacity to demand hadd. If the slander directly targets a non-muhsan person, the son cannot demand because there is no complete shame. This is because the master and father are not punished through their subordinates/children. Analogous rules in qisas are cited. However, if the woman has a son from another husband, that son can demand because there is no preventing relationship. The passage ends with a hadith warning of punishment in the Hereafter for such false accusations.

Key Terms
مانع (māni): A preventing factor; here, the master-slave or father-son relationship prevents the claim.

According to the Hanafi school, can a son demand hadd against his father for slandering the son's free Muslim mother?
A) Yes, because the mother is free and Muslim.
B) No, because a father is not punished due to his son.
C) Yes, but only if he is the only son.
D) No, because the mother must also be a slave.

Key Takeaway

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Son's Right to Demand Hadd for Qadhf Against Accuser of Muhsan Father
Ruling on the son's right to demand hadd for qadhf against his father's accuser

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the son's right to demand hadd for qadhf and analyze Imam Zufar's opposing argument using the concept of ta'yir al-kamal.

Core Idea
The complete shame of accusing a muhsan father extends to his son, enabling the son's hadd claim.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the right to demand the hadd punishment for slanderous accusation (qadhf). The majority of the Hanafi school, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the son of a muhsan (a person meeting the conditions of ihsan) can demand hadd against the accuser even if the son himself is a disbeliever or a slave. Imam Zufar, a prominent Hanafi jurist, disagreed, arguing that the shame does not directly reach the son. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the majority Hanafi school holds: the son can demand hadd even if he is a kafir or slave.
The right is not through inheritance but based on direct harm.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds that the son cannot demand hadd because the shame reaches the father, not the son.
His reasoning is that the son's right would only be through inheritance, which is inapplicable.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's dalil: the accuser's ta'yir is directed at the father; the son is not directly shamed.
Thus, no direct right for the son.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority argue that the complete ta'yir (ta'yir al-kamal) is achieved only because the father is muhsan; this complete shame then returns to the son.
The son's eligibility to claim is not affected by his disbelief or slavery.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: according to the majority, the son can file a hadd claim; according to Zufar, he cannot.
The mufta bihi position is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَعْنَى لِوُجُوعِ الْعَارِ إِلَيْهِ وَ لَيْسَ طَرِيقُهُ الْإِرْثَ عِنْدَنَا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا كَانَ مُتَنَاوِلاً لَهُ صُورَةً وَمَعْنًى وَلَنَا إِنَّهُ عَيَّرَهُ بِقَذْفِ مُحْصَنٍ فَيَأْخُذُهُ بِالْحَدِّ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْإِحْصَانَ فِي الَّذِي يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الزِّنَاءِ شَرْطٌ لِيَقَعَ تَعْيِيرًا عَلَى الْكَمَالِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ هَذَا التَّعْيِيرُ الْكَامِلُ إِلَى وَلَدِهِ وَالْكُفْرُ لَا يَقْدَحُ فِي أَهْلِيَّةِ الِاسْتِحْقَاقِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا تَنَاوَلَهُ الْقَذْفُ نَفْسَهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوجَدِ التَّعْيِيرُ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ لِفَقْدِ الْإِحْصَانِ فِي الْمَنْسُوبِ إِلَى الزِّنَاءِ
Meaning: because the shame returns to him, but it is not through inheritance according to us, so it becomes like when it includes him in form and meaning. And our proof: he indeed shamed him by accusing a muhsan, so he (the son) takes him with the hadd. And this is because being muhsan in the one attributed to zina is a condition for it to be a complete shaming, then this complete shaming returns to his son. And disbelief does not detract from eligibility to claim. Unlike when the accusation directly targets the son himself, because in that case the complete shaming is not found due to the lack of muhsan in the attributed one.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi argument in a dispute with Imam Zufar. The ruling: if a person accused of zina is muhsan (free, adult, Muslim, married), his son has the right to demand the hadd (Quranic punishment) against the accuser, even if the son himself is a disbeliever or a slave. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that the shame does not directly affect the son; rather it affects the father, and the son's right would only come through inheritance, which does not apply. The Hanafi response (ولنا) is that the accuser shamed the son indirectly by accusing his father. The condition of ihsan on the father is necessary for the ta'yir (shaming) to be complete; if the father were not muhsan, the accusation would not be as shameful. The complete shame then extends to the son. The son's disbelief does not prevent him from having the right to demand hadd, because this right is based on direct harm (shame) and not on religious capacity. However, if the accusation directly touched the son himself (i.e., he was the accused), he would not have the right to demand because the condition of ihsan is absent in that case. This highlights that the hadd for qadhf serves to remove shame from the victim and his family.

Key Terms
مُحْصَن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has consummated a valid marriage, making the accusation of zina particularly grave.
تَعْيِير (ta'yir): Shaming or reproaching, specifically in the context of qadhf, where the accusation of zina is intended to disgrace the accused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (majority), the son of a muhsan accused of zina can demand the hadd of qadhf against the accuser even if the son is a disbeliever because:
A) The right is inherited from his father.
B) The complete shaming (ta'yir) directed at the father extends to the son directly.
C) The son always has the right to claim on behalf of his father regardless.
D) Disbelief does not affect eligibility for hadd claims.

Key Takeaway
The complete shame of accusing a muhsan father extends to his son, establishing the son's right to demand hadd for qadhf irrespective of his own status as disbeliever or slave.

Slave and Son Cannot Demand Hadd for Qadhf of Free Mother
Ruling on the inadmissibility of hadd claims by a slave against master or son against father for qadhf of the mother.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave cannot demand hadd for qadhf against his master for accusing his free mother, and explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) from the rule of qisas.

Core Idea
No hadd for master or father in claims arising from slave or son.

This passage presents a specific ruling within the law of qadhf (false accusation of zina). While normally any free Muslim has the right to demand the hadd punishment against an accuser, this right is blocked when the accuser stands in a relationship of authority over the claimant. The text uses a clear analogical argument from the well-known rule in qisas: a father is not executed for killing his son, nor a master for killing his slave. The same logic applies to hadd claims for qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings stated
Read the first part of the Arabic: a slave cannot demand hadd from his master for accusing his free mother; a son cannot demand hadd from his father for accusing his free Muslim mother. Note the conditions: the mother must be free and (for the son's case) Muslim.
2
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
The text provides an analogy: the master/father is not punished due to his slave/son, just as in qisas he is not executed for killing them. Identify the asl (qisas rule), the far' (qadhf claim), and the illa (relationship of authority).
The hadith 'لا يُقتل والد بولده' is the evidence for the asl.
3
Understand the illa and its scope
The illa is that punishment is not established when the claim arises from someone under the authority of the accused. This preventer (mani') blocks the right to demand hadd.
The illa is jaliyyah (manifest) because it is derived from a clear textual rule.
4
Recognize the exception
The text adds: if the mother has a son from another man (not the master or father), that son can demand hadd. The preventer is absent, so the original right to demand hadd applies.
This confirms the rule: the preventer is the specific relationship of authority.
5
State the underlying principle
The principle is that legal claims arising from those under one's authority do not give rise to criminal punishment against the authority figure, whether in qisas or hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ مَوْلَاهُ بِقَذْفِ أُمِّهِ الْحُرَّةِ وَلَا لِلِابْنِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ آبَاهُ بِقَذْفِ أُمِّهِ الْحُرَّةِ الْمُسْلِمَةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَوْلَى لَا يُعَاقَبُ بِسَبَبِ عَبْدِهِ وَكَذَا الْأَبُ بِسَبَبِ ابْنِهِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقَادُ الْوَالِدُ وَلَا السَّيِّدُ بِعَبْدِهِ وَلَوْ كَانَ لَهَا ابْنٌ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ لَهُ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ لِتَحَقُّقِ السَّبَبِ وَالْعِدَامِ الْمَانِعِ
And a slave does not have the right to demand from his master for his accusation of his free mother, nor does a son have the right to demand from his father for his accusation of his free Muslim mother, because the master is not punished due to his slave, and likewise the father due to his son. For this reason, the father is not subjected to qisas for his son, nor the master for his slave. And if she has a son from someone else, he has the right to demand due to the existence of the cause and the absence of the preventer.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the right to demand the hadd of qadhf when the accuser is the master of the victim's son, or the father of the victim's son. Specifically: if a master accuses his slave's free mother of zina, the slave cannot demand hadd against his master. Similarly, if a father accuses his son's free Muslim mother (i.e., the son's mother, who may be the father's wife or ex-wife), the son cannot demand hadd against his father. The reasoning is that a master is not subjected to punishment solely because of a claim from his slave; the slave's right is subordinate. Analogously, a father is not punished due to his son. This principle is supported by the rule in qisas: a father is not executed for killing his son, nor is a master executed for killing his slave. However, an exception exists: if the woman (the accused mother) has a son from a different man (not the master or the father), that son can demand hadd against the accuser. This is because the cause (the qadhf) is fully present, and the preventer (the relationship of slavery or paternity) is absent.

Key Terms
مَوْلَى (mawla): Master or patron, in this context the owner of the slave.
قَذْف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, which of the following statements is correct?
A) A slave can always demand hadd against his master for accusing his mother.
B) A son can demand hadd against his father for accusing his mother only if the mother is a slave.
C) A slave cannot demand hadd against his master for accusing his free mother.
D) A son can demand hadd against his father for accusing his mother regardless of her status.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school blocks the right to demand hadd for qadhf when the accuser is the master of the claimant or the father, based on the principle that punishment is not exacted from those in authority due to claims arising from subordinates.

Death of the Accused Voids Hadd for Qadhf: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on death of accused voiding hadd of qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the effect of the accused's death on the hadd of qadhf and explain the underlying reason (haqq Allah vs haqq al-'abd) that leads to differences with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The death of the victim voids the hadd because God's right dominates over the individual's right.

This lesson explores a key juristic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does the death of the person accused of slander (qadhf) nullify the prescribed hadd punishment? The answer depends on whether the hadd is seen primarily as a right of God (haqq Allah) or a right of the individual (haqq al-'abd). We will analyze the Hanafi reasoning and contrast it with the Shafi'i perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine what happens to the hadd when the accused dies. The Hanafi position is that the hadd becomes void entirely; even if part was executed, the remainder is void. The Shafi'i position is that the hadd does not become void and can be inherited or pursued by heirs.
The disagreement is not about the existence of the two aspects but about which aspect dominates.
2
Analyze the two aspects of the hadd
The hadd has a personal benefit: removing shame from the victim (haqq al-'abd). It also has a societal deterrent: protecting the community from corruption (haqq Allah). Recognize that both aspects are acknowledged by both schools.
3
Examine the conflict and each school's weighting
When the aspects conflict, Shafi'i gives priority to the individual's right because the victim suffers personally and God is self-sufficient. Hanafis give priority to God's right because the servant's right is subsumed under God's care, and the servant has no authority over God's rights except by deputyship.
The Hanafi argument is that the master (God) automatically takes care of the servant's right, so the servant's right is not lost; it is observed through God's right.
4
Derive the subsidiary differences
From the principle of dominance, four subsidiary rulings follow: (1) inheritance – not allowed for God's rights; (2) pardon – the victim's pardon does not affect the hadd; (3) substitution – not allowed; (4) merger – multiple accusations merge into one hadd. Note that Abu Yusuf held a different view on pardon.
These furu' are deduced from the same foundational principle.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text concludes that the first view (God's right dominant) is more apparent. This is the mufta bihi position. Understand the epistemological weight: it is from the zahir al-riwayah.
Even though some Hanafi scholars (like Abu Yusuf on pardon) and a minority of later scholars favor the servant's right, the dominant Hanafi position is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَذَفَ غَيْرَهُ فَمَاتَ الْمَقْذُوفُ بَطَلَ الْحَدُّ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَبْطُلُ وَلَوْ مَاتَ بَعْدَ مَا أُقِيمَ بَعْضُ الْحَدِّ بَطَلَ الْبَاقِي عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لَهُ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ يُورَثُ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يُورَثُ وَلَا خِلَافَ أَنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّ الشَّرْعِ وَحَقَّ الْعَبْدِ فَإِنَّهُ شُرِعَ لِدَفْعِ الْعَارِ عَنِ الْمَقْذُوفِ وَهُوَ الَّذِي يُنْتَفَعُ بِهِ عَلَى الْخُصُوصِ فَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُ شُرِعَ زَاجِرًا وَمِنْهُ سُمِّيَ حَدًّا وَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنْ شَرْعِ الزَّاجِرِ إِخْلَاءُ الْعَالَمِ عَنِ الْفَسَادِ وَهَذَا إِيَاءُ حَقِّ الشَّرْعِ وَبِكُلِّ ذَلِكَ تَشْهَدُ الْأَحْكَامُ وَإِذَا تَعَارَضَتِ الْجِهَّتَانِ فَالشَّافِعِيُّ مَالَ إِلَى تَغْلِيبِ حَقِّ الْعَبْدِ تَقْدِيمًا لِحَقِّ الْعَبْدِ بِاعْتِبَارِ حَاجَتِهِ وَغِنَاءِ الشَّرْعِ وَنَحْنُ صِرْنَا إِلَى تَغْلِيبِ حَقِّ الشَّرْعِ لِأَنَّ مَا لِلْعَبْدِ مِنَ الْحَقِّ يَتَوَلَّاهُ مَوْلَاهُ فَيَصِيرُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ مَرْعِيًّا بِهِ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ عَكْسُهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا وَلَايَةَ لِلْعَبْدِ فِي اسْتِيفَاءِ حُقُوقِ الشَّرْعِ إِلَّا نِيَابَةً وَهَذَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ الْمَشْهُورُ الَّذِي يَتَخَرَّجُ عَلَيْهِ الْفُرُوعُ الْمُخْتَلَفُ فِيهَا مِنْهَا الْإِرْثُ إِذِ الْإِرْثُ يَجْرِي فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ لَا فِي حُقُوقِ الشَّرْعِ وَمِنْهَا الْعَفْوُ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُّ عَفْوُ الْمَقْذُوفِ عِنْدَنَا وَيَصِحُّ عِنْدَهُ وَمِنْهَا أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ الِاعْتِيَاضُ عَنْهُ وَيَجْرِي فِيهِ التَّدَاخُلُ وَعِنْدَهُ لَا يَجْرِي وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِي الْعَفْوِ مِثْلُ قَوْلِ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَمِنْ أَصْحَابِنَا مَنْ قَالَ إِنَّ الْغَالِبَ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَ خَرَجَتِ الْأَحْكَامُ وَالْأَوَّلُ أَظْهَرُ
And whoever accuses another, then the accused dies, the hadd is void. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not become void. And if he dies after some of the hadd has been established, the remainder is void according to us, contrary to him. This is based on the fact that it is inherited according to him, while according to us it is not inherited. There is no disagreement that it contains a right of God and a right of the servant. For it is legislated to remove shame from the accused, and he is the one who specifically benefits from it; from this aspect it is a right of the servant. Then, it is legislated as a deterrent, and from this it is called hadd. The objective of legislating the deterrent is to clear the world of corruption, and this is the sign of the right of God. And all these rulings bear witness. When the two aspects conflict, al-Shafi'i inclined to giving weight to the right of the servant, prioritizing the servant's right due to his need and God's self-sufficiency. We (Hanafis) have adopted giving weight to the right of God because whatever right the servant has, his Master (God) takes charge of it, so the servant's right becomes observed through it, and not so the opposite, because the servant has no authority in exacting the rights of God except by deputyship. This is the famous principle from which the various subsidiary issues are derived. Among them: inheritance, since inheritance applies to the rights of servants, not to the rights of God. And among them: pardon, so the pardon of the accused is not valid according to us, but is valid according to him. And among them: that substitution for it is not allowed and merging applies in it, while according to him merging does not apply. And from Abu Yusuf, regarding pardon, a view similar to that of al-Shafi'i. And among our companions are those who say that the dominant aspect is the servant's right, and the rulings are derived accordingly. But the first (God's right dominant) is more apparent.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of the death of the accused (مقذوف) on the hadd punishment for qadhf. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that if the accused dies before the hadd is executed, the hadd is entirely void. Even if part of the hadd has been executed, the remaining part is also void. The Shafi'i position is that the hadd is not void; it can be inherited and demanded by the heirs. The basis of the dispute is the nature of the right involved in qadhf: is it predominantly a right of God (حق الله) or a right of the servant (حق العبد)? The text explains that the hadd has two aspects: it serves to remove shame from the victim (a servant's right) and it serves as a deterrent to protect society (a God's right). When these conflict, Shafi'i gives precedence to the servant's right, considering the victim's need and God's independence from need. The Hanafis give precedence to God's right, because God (the true Master) takes care of the servant's right—the servant's right is not lost but is subsumed under God's overarching right. The servant has no authority to exact God's rights except as a deputy. Consequently, various subsidiary rulings differ between the schools: (1) Inheritance: Shafi'i allows the hadd to be inherited; Hanafi does not. (2) Pardon: According to Hanafi, the victim's pardon does not nullify the hadd (since it is God's right), but Shafi'i holds it does. (3) Compensation: Hanafi holds that substitution/composition is not allowed, and multiple accusations merge into one hadd (تداخل); Shafi'i holds composition is allowed and they do not merge. The text also records that Imam Abu Yusuf held a view similar to Shafi'i regarding pardon. Some Hanafi scholars opined that the servant's right is dominant, but the first (dominance of God's right) is more apparent.

Key Terms
حَقُّ الشَّرْع (haqq al-shar'): The right of God (the lawgiver) in the punishment, i.e., the deterrent aspect that benefits society.
حَقُّ الْعَبْد (haqq al-'abd): The right of the individual (the victim) in the punishment, i.e., removal of personal shame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the victim of qadhf dies before the hadd is fully executed, what happens to the remaining punishment?
A) The hadd is void completely.
B) The hadd is reduced proportionally.
C) The hadd must be completed by the heirs.
D) The hadd is commuted to a fine.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the hadd of qadhf is void upon the victim's death because it is treated as a right of God, which does not transmit to heirs and cannot be pardoned by the victim after death.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

8 min
Retraction from Confession of Qadhf is Ineffective
Ruling on retraction after confessing to qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction from a confession of qadhf, distinguish it from retraction from pure divine rights, and explain the rational basis for the distinction.

Core Idea
Retraction from qadhf confession is ineffective because the slandered person's right bars it.

In Hanafi criminal law, a confession (iqrar) can be a powerful tool for establishing guilt. However, once a person confesses to a crime that involves a personal right of another individual, the confessor cannot simply withdraw that confession. This lesson examines the ruling on retraction from a confession of qadhf (false accusation of unchastity) and the rationale that distinguishes it from confessions to purely divine offenses.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on retraction from confession of qadhf
Identify the specific ruling: retraction (ruju') is not accepted (la yuqbal). The confession stands and the hadd penalty is still applicable.
This ruling is explicit in the text: 'whoever confesses to qadhf then retracts, his retraction is not accepted.'
2
Identify the key distinction: haqq Allah vs. haqq al-‘abd
The text contrasts qadhf with offenses that are 'purely the right of Allah' (khalis haqq Allah), such as drinking wine. For those, retraction is accepted because no human individual has a personal right to contradict the retraction.
The distinction hinges on the presence of a personal right (haqq al-‘abd) in the offense.
3
Explain the rationale for not accepting retraction in qadhf
The maqdhuf (slandered person) has a right in the hadd—specifically, to have the penalty executed to clear his name. When the confessor retracts, the maqdhuf can 'contradict' (yukadhdhib) the retraction, i.e., insist on the original confession. Thus the confessor's retraction is not allowed because it would nullify this established right.
This is a rational (aqli) proof: the existence of a contradictory right prevents retraction.
4
Compare with a pure haqq Allah offense (shurb al-khamr)
If a person confesses to drinking wine and then retracts, the retraction is accepted because there is no human plaintiff with a personal right. Only Allah's right is involved, and the confessor can repent and withdraw his confession.
This comparison illustrates the boundary: the ruling changes when a human right is present.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, if retraction were accepted, the maqdhuf would lose his right to have the hadd enforced, which would leave his reputation unjustly tarnished. Therefore, Hanafi law protects the maqdhuf's right by rejecting the retraction.
This protection is a core reason for the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَدْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ لأَنَّ لِلْمَقْدُوفِ فِيهِ حَقًّا فَيُكَذِّبُهُ فِي الرُّجُوعِ بِخِلَافِ مَاهُوَ خَالِصُ حَقِّ اللَّهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَكْذُوبَ لَهُ فِيهِ
Whoever confesses to qadhf and then retracts, his retraction is not accepted, because the slandered person has a right in it, so he would contradict his retraction. Unlike what is purely the right of Allah, for there is no one to contradict him in it.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding retraction (ruju') from a confession (iqrar) of qadhf. In Hanafi law, if a person confesses to having falsely accused another of zina (qadhf) and then retracts that confession, the retraction is not accepted. The reason is that the slandered person (maqdhuf) has a right in the matter—specifically, his right to have the hadd executed to clear his name. This right is established by the confession, and the maqdhuf can therefore contradict (yukadhdhib) the confessor's retraction, because the retraction would negate his established right. In contrast, if the confession pertains to an act that is purely a right of Allah (khalis haqq Allah), such as drinking wine (shurb al-khamr), retraction from a confession is accepted because no human individual has a personal right that opposes it. Only Allah's right is involved, and repentance is possible. Thus, the distinction hinges on whether the offense involves a personal right of another person. Qadhf involves both a right of Allah and a right of the individual (as seen in the previous lesson), but the confession itself gives the slandered person a claim. Therefore, retraction is ineffective.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A juridical confession or admission, typically made before a court.
رجع (raja'a): To retract or withdraw a statement or confession.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right belonging to a human individual, such as the right to demand punishment for a wrong committed against him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is retraction from a confession of qadhf not accepted in Hanafi law?
A) Because qadhf is a major sin and repentance is not allowed.
B) Because the slandered person has a right in the hadd, so he would contradict the retraction.
C) Because the confession is considered an oath that cannot be broken.
D) Because the judge does not have the authority to accept retraction.

Key Takeaway
Retraction from a confession of qadhf is ineffective because it would violate the slandered person's established right to have the hadd executed.

Calling an Arab 'Nabati' Does Not Incur Hadd
Ruling on the hadd penalty for insulting an Arab as 'Nabati'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on calling an Arab 'Nabati' and explain why it does not incur the hadd of qadhf.

Core Idea
Calling an Arab 'Nabati' is an insult, not an accusation of zina — qadhf requires imputation of unchastity.

The hadd penalty for qadhf (false accusation of unlawful intercourse) is severe. However, not every insult qualifies. In this lesson, we examine a specific case: someone calls an Arab 'Nabati' (a derogatory term for non-Arab). Does this trigger the fixed punishment? The Hanafi ruling is clear — it does not. Understanding why clarifies the precise legal scope of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is saying 'O Nabati' to an Arab. The question is whether this constitutes qadhf, which is falsely accusing someone of zina.
Qadhf is a specific crime with a fixed hadd penalty.
2
State the ruling
The text rules: 'lam yuhadd' — he is not subjected to hadd. Thus, no fixed penalty applies.
The ruling is negative: no hadd.
3
Analyze the reason (ta'lil)
The reason given: 'because it is intended as a comparison in bad character or lack of eloquence.' The term does not imply unchastity; it is a general insult about character or speech.
The intention ('yurada') matters in determining whether it is qadhf.
4
Apply to similar cases
The text extends the same ruling to saying 'You are not an Arab' — also not qadhf for the same reason.
Other insults that do not explicitly or implicitly accuse zina are similarly not qadhf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِلْعَرْبِي يَا نِبْطِيُّ لَمْ يُحَدَّ لِأَنَّهُ يُرَادُ بِهِ التَّشْبِيْهُ فِي الْإِخْلَافِ أَوْ عَدَمِ الْفَصَاحَةِ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ لَسْتَ بِعَرْبِي لِمَا قُلْنَا

Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling that calling an Arab 'Nabati' (a term for non-Arab, often used derogatorily) does not incur the hadd penalty for qadhf (false accusation of zina). The reason is that the term is understood to be an insult implying bad character or lack of eloquence (fasahah), not a direct accusation of unchastity. Qadhf specifically requires the imputation of unlawful sexual intercourse. Since 'Nabati' does not explicitly or impliedly convey that, it is not considered qadhf. Similarly, telling an Arab 'You are not an Arab' is not qadhf for the same reason. Such insults may be subject to ta'zir (discretionary punishment) if they cause harm, but they do not carry the fixed hadd penalty. The passage emphasizes that the contextual meaning (what is intended by the speaker) is relevant in determining whether an utterance constitutes qadhf.

Key Terms
نبطي (Nabati): A Nabataean; historically, non-Arab inhabitants of the region, often used disparagingly to imply coarseness or lack of Arab lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Yes, if the person is offended.
D) No, because the term 'Nabati' is not known.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly limits qadhf to accusations of zina; general insults like 'Nabati' are not subject to hadd but may be punished by ta'zir.

Forgiveness, Compensation, and Tadakhul in Hadd al-Qadhf
Explains Hanafi position on victim's forgiveness, compensation, and tadakhul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school holds that forgiveness and compensation do not nullify hadd al-qadhf and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the haqq Allah vs. haqq al-'abd framework.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd al-qadhf is a right of Allah—victim's forgiveness does not drop the punishment.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute: can the victim of false accusation forgive the hadd punishment or accept compensation? The Hanafi school argues that because the right is predominantly Allah's (haqq Allah), personal forgiveness cannot waive it, and tadakhul (one hadd for multiple accusations) applies. Understanding this distinction reveals how Hanafi usul categorizes legal rights and determines the enforceability of hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and note the three distinct rulings: (1) victim's forgiveness does not nullify hadd, (2) taking compensation is impermissible, (3) tadakhul applies when multiple are accused.
These all stem from the same principle: the right of Allah is dominant.
2
Trace the Hanafi reasoning
The passage explains that because hadd is a 'haqq Allah' (right of Allah), the victim cannot waive it. Compensation is also impermissible for the same reason.
The term 'haqq Allah' is pivotal—it means the punishment serves a public interest.
3
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i views the hadd as primarily a personal right (haqq al-'abd), so the victim can forgive, accept compensation, and no tadakhul occurs.
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, the ruler must enforce hadd even if the victim forgives.
4
Examine intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Yusuf has a narration aligning with Shafi'i, and some later Hanafi scholars also favored the victim's right. However, the majority of mashayikh adopted the first view, calling it 'azhar' (more apparent).
This illustrates that even within a school, there can be minority views, but the mufta bihi is the dominant one.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the hadd is applied regardless of the victim's wishes; under Shafi'i, the victim can drop it or settle for compensation.
Tadakhul saves resources: one hadd for multiple accusations, while Shafi'i would require separate hadd for each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد القذف
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم... ہے کہ جس پر قذف لگائی گئی ہے اگر وہ خود معاف کر دے تو ہمارے نزدیک صحیح نہیں ہو گا یعنی حق شرع ہونے کی بناء پر اس پر حد جاری ہوکر رہے گی۔ لیکن امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ کے نزدیک معاف کرنا صحیح ہوگا۔ ۳۔ یہ کہ قذف کا عوض لے لینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ یعنی ہمارے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں حق الہی غالب ہے اور اس میں تداخل جاری ہوگا۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے کئی آدمیوں پر تہمت لگائی تو سب کے لئے ایک ہی حد لگائی جائے گی۔ لیکن امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس طرح داخل نہیں ہوگا (بلکہ ہر ایک کے لئے علیحدہ حد جاری کی جائے گی )۔ اس معاف کر دینے کی صورت میں ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے بھی ایک روایت امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے قول کے مثل منقول ہے اور ہمارے اصحاب حنفیہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم میں سے بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ اس صورت میں بندہ کا حق غالب ہے اورمثل امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علی سے مل احکام بیان کئے ہیں۔ لیکن قول اول یہی اظہر ہے۔ ف۔ اور عامہ مشائخ نے اس کو اختیار فرمایا ہے۔ (النہایہ) تشریح و من قذف غيره فمات المقذوف بطل الحدوقال الشافعي لا يبطل ولومات .... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. The commentary says: If the person who was accused of adultery forgives, then in our view (Hanafi) it is not valid, meaning because it is a right of Allah, the hadd will be carried out. But according to Imam al-Shafi'i, forgiveness is valid. 3: Taking compensation for qadhf is not permissible, in our view it is not permissible because the right of Allah is dominant, and tadakhul (interference) will occur: if someone accuses multiple people, one hadd will be applied for all. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, tadakhul does not occur (rather a separate hadd for each). Regarding forgiveness, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf similar to al-Shafi'i, and some of our Hanafi scholars said that in this case the right of the servant is dominant and gave rulings like al-Shafi'i. But the first opinion is more apparent (azhar), and the majority of mashayikh have adopted it. (al-Nihayah) Commentary: 'And whoever accuses another, then the accused dies, the hadd is nullified, and al-Shafi'i said it is not nullified...' etc., the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage discusses three interconnected rulings in the chapter of hadd al-qadhf (punishment for false accusation of adultery). First: The victim's forgiveness does not nullify the hadd in the Hanafi school because the right involved is primarily from the rights of Allah (haqqu Allah), unlike Shafi'i who sees it as a personal right. Second: Taking monetary compensation in lieu of hadd is impermissible for the same reason—the divine right is dominant. Third: Tadakhul (confluence) applies: if a person falsely accuses multiple individuals, only one hadd is imposed, not multiple. Imam Shafi'i disagrees on all three counts. There is an intra-Hanafi narration from Abu Yusuf aligning with Shafi'i, and some Hanafi scholars favored the servant's right, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) remains that the divine right is predominant. The commentary ends with a reference to another ruling about the death of the accused.

Key Terms
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for falsely accusing a chaste person of adultery or fornication.
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right that belongs primarily to Allah, meaning it cannot be waived by individuals.
تداخل (tadakhul): Interference or confluence: when multiple violations result in a single penalty.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right that belongs to a human being, which they can waive or settle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The hadd is dropped because the victim forgave.
B) The hadd is still carried out because it is a right of Allah.
C) The hadd is reduced to ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
D) The hadd is converted into compensation (diyah).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd al-qadhf is a right of Allah, so victim forgiveness and compensation are invalid, and tadakhul applies for multiple accusations.

Retraction of Confession in Qadhf: The Victim's Right Prevents Retraction
Ruling on retracting a qadhf confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on retracting a qadhf confession and explain why retraction is not accepted in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Retraction of qadhf confession is rejected because the victim's personal right overrides the confessor's recantation.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling in the law of qadhf (false accusation of adultery): whether a confessor can retract his confession. The passage establishes that retraction is not accepted, and the key distinction is the presence of a human right (haqq al-'abd) which gives the victim standing to belie the retraction. Understanding this distinction clarifies how Hanafi fiqh balances divine rights and individual rights in hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Confessing to qadhf and then retracting. What is the ruling? The retraction is not accepted, meaning the hadd will be enforced.
The ruling is clear: retraction is rejected.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the existence of the victim's right (haqq al-'abd). The victim can belie the retraction because the confession established a right for him.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the nature of rights.
3
Understand the distinction from pure divine rights
Contrast with cases where only Allah's right is involved (e.g., confession to drinking wine). There, retraction is accepted because no human has a right to belie.
This contrast highlights the importance of the victim's personal stake.
4
Note the consequence
Since retraction is not accepted, the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes) becomes enforceable. The confession alone is sufficient for the hadd to be wajib.
The victim's right is prioritized over the confessor's recantation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قذف کے اقرار سے رجوع کا حکم
وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَدْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ لأَنَّ لِلْمَقْدُوفِ فِيهِ حَقًّا فَيُكَذِّبُهُ فِي الرُّجُوعِ بِخِلَافِ مَاهُوَ خَالِصُ حَقِّ اللَّهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَكْذُوبَ لَهُ فِيهِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے دوسرے پر زنا کا الزام لگایا پھر اپنے الزام سے رجوع کرلیا تو اس کا رجوع کرنا قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس الزام کی وجہ سے جس پر الزام لگایا گیا ہے اس کا حق بھی متعلق ہو گیا ہے تو وہ اس کے رجوع میں اس کی تکذیب کرے گا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جو خالص حق الہی ہو کیونکہ الزام اس کے رجوع کرنے پر کوئی انسان کی تکذیب کرنے والا نہ ہو گا۔

تشريح و من اقر بالقذف ثم رجع لم يقبل رجوعه لان للمقذوف فيه حقا فيكذب الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Ruling on retracting confession of qadhf. And whoever confesses to qadhf then retracts, his retraction is not accepted because the victim has a right in it, so he (the victim) will belie him in the retraction, contrary to what is purely a right of Allah, because there is no one to belie him in it. Translation: And the person who accuses another of adultery then retracts, his retraction is not accepted because the victim has a right, so he will belie him. Unlike the case of purely Allah's right, where no human belies him. Commentary: 'And whoever confesses to qadhf then retracts, his retraction is not accepted because the victim has a right, so he belies him...' the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This is a ruling on retracting a confession of false accusation (qadhf). The matn states that once a person confesses to qadhf, his retraction is not accepted. The reason is that the victim (the one accused) now has a personal right (haqq al-'abd) established through the confession. The victim can claim that the confession was true, and his claim is given weight because the confessor cannot unilaterally revoke the victim's right. This is contrasted with matters that are purely the rights of Allah, such as confession to drinking wine, where retraction is accepted because no human's right is involved. The commentary simply confirms this ruling.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession, admission of guilt.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction, withdrawal of a statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the judge has already pronounced the hadd.
D) Because it is a purely divine right.

Key Takeaway
In qadhf, the victim's right (haqq al-'abd) prevents retraction of a confession, making the hadd enforceable.

Core Idea
Insulting an Arab as 'Nabati' is not qadhf because it implies lack of eloquence, not an accusation of zina.

This lesson addresses a specific case within the law of qadhf: does calling an Arab a 'Nabati' (a term for non-Arab, used as an insult) trigger the fixed punishment for false accusation of adultery? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the intention and linguistic implication of the term. Understanding this distinction helps you see the strict limits of the hadd punishment.

Identify the act: a person says 'O Nabati' to an Arab. The ruling: no hadd al-qadhf is imposed.

3

Why 'Son of Sky Water' Is Not Qadhf
Ruling that calling someone 'Ibn Ma' al-Sama'' is praise, not slander

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that calling someone 'Ibn Ma' al-Sama'' does not incur hadd al-qadhf, and distinguish between literal and customary meaning in hudud.

Core Idea
Customary usage (urf), not literal meaning, determines whether a phrase constitutes qadhf.

When someone says 'O son of sky water,' it might sound insulting if taken literally, but Arabic custom uses it as high praise. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that such an expression is not qadhf, and we explore the principle that customary context overrides literal wording in hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression
Recognize the phrase 'Ibn Ma' al-Sama'' and consider its literal implication of questioning lineage.
Literal meaning could be construed as an accusation of illegitimate birth.
2
Determine customary usage
In Arab culture, this phrase is used to praise generosity, purity, and nobility.
Custom (urf) gives the phrase a laudatory meaning.
3
Apply Hanafi principle in hudud
Hudud are suspended by doubt (shubha). The ambiguity between literal and customary meaning creates doubt.
Thus, no hadd is applied.
4
Support with prophetic precedent
The Prophet used this phrase for the descendants of Isma'il, confirming it as praise.
Hadith in Bukhari: 'This is your mother, O sons of sky water.'
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, saying 'Ibn Ma' al-Sama'' is not qadhf, and no hadd is incurred.
The ruling is based on urf and prophetic usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی کو ابن ماء السماء کہنے سے حد کا حکم
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِرَجُلٍ يَا ابْنَ مَاءِ السَّمَاءِ فَلَيْسَ بِقَاذِفٍ لِأَنَّهُ يُرَادُ بِهِ التَّشْبِيْة فِى الْجُودِ وَالسَّمَاحَةِ وَالصَّفَاءِ لِأَنَّ مَاءَ السَّمَاءِ لَقِبَ بِهِ لِصَفَائِهِ وَسَخَائِهِ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے سے کہا او آسمانی پانی کے بچے تو اس سے تہمت لگانا ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس لفظ سے مقصود اس کی تعریف یعنی بخشش و جواں مردی و صفائی میں تشبیہ مقصود ہوتی ہے ۔ نکہ آسان پانی کا لقب صفائی وسخاوت کی وجہ سے ہے (ف۔ یعنی جیسے آسمانی پانی گندگی اور میل و کچیل سے صاف اور بہت زیادہ برستا ہے اسی طرح اس شخص کا نطفہ خالص ہے۔ حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ نے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث جو حضرت اسمعیل علیہ السلام کی والدہ ہاجرہ کے بارے میں نقل کی ہے۔ کہ فهذه امك يا بلد ماء السماء یعنی اے آسمانی پانی کی اولاد بھی تمہاری والدہ
ہیں۔ (رواہ البخاری)
اس سے ظاہر ہے کہ یہ لفظ تعریف کے طور پر ہے۔ برائی کے طور پر نہیں)۔
تشریح.... و من قال للعربي يا نبطى لم يحد لانه يراد به التشبيه الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Ruling on saying 'Son of sky water'. And whoever says to a man 'O son of sky water' is not a slanderer (qadhif) because it is intended as a comparison in generosity, magnanimity, and purity, because 'sky water' is a title given for its purity and generosity. Translation: If someone says to another 'O son of sky water', slander is not established because the intended meaning is praise—comparison in generosity, bravery, and purity. Sky water is called so for its purity and generosity. (So, just as sky water is pure from dirt and filth and pours abundantly, similarly this person's sperm is pure.) Hadith: Abu Hurairah narrated from the Prophet about Hajar, mother of Isma'il: 'So this is your mother, O sons of sky water' (Bukhari). This shows the word is used for praise, not blame. Commentary: 'And whoever says to an Arab 'O Nabati' is not subjected to hadd...' the meaning is clear.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
The phrase 'Ibn Ma' al-Sama'' (son of rainwater) is historically used as a title of praise among Arabs, implying nobility, generosity, and purity. Even though it could be misconstrued as implying a birth from water, the customary usage is laudatory. Therefore, saying this to someone is not qadhf. The text supports this with a hadith where the Prophet addresses the descendants of Isma'il as 'bani ma' al-sama'' in a praiseworthy context. The commentary reaffirms the principle that context and customary usage determine whether an expression is qadhf.

Key Terms
ابن ماء السماء (ibn ma' al-sama'): Literally 'son of sky water'; a phrase meaning a noble, generous person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a phrase used by the Prophet, so it is always lawful.
B) The phrase is ambiguous and customary usage is praise, creating doubt.
C) The listener must be a specific person.
D) The speaker must have no intention.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, customary usage (urf) determines whether a statement is qadhf; literal meaning alone is insufficient for hudud.

Attributing to Uncle, Maternal Uncle, or Stepfather: Not Qadhf
Ruling that calling someone son of uncle/stepfather is not slander

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that attributing someone to a non-biological father relative is not qadhf and explain the three proofs (Quran, hadith, custom).

Core Idea
Calling someone 'son of uncle' is not slander because Islamic usage extends 'father' to uncles and stepfathers.

In Hanafi law, qadhf (false accusation of illicit relations) carries a prescribed hadd punishment. But not every misattribution of lineage qualifies. This lesson examines a specific case: when someone attributes another to a relative like an uncle or stepfather—terms that are broadly considered 'father' in Islamic tradition. The text provides three proofs to show why such statements fall outside qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is attributing someone to his paternal uncle (amm), maternal uncle (khal), or stepfather (zawj al-umm). The ruling is that this is not qadhf—no hadd punishment applies.
Focus on the act, not the intent; the ruling is based on linguistic usage.
2
Recognize the three categories
The text lists three relatives each called 'father' in a broad sense: paternal uncle (by Quran), maternal uncle (by hadith), and stepfather (by custom of upbringing).
These are the only three; other relatives like cousin do not have this ruling.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof for paternal uncle
The verse (2:133) refers to Ibrahim, Isma'il, and Ishaq as 'fathers' (aba') of Ya'qub. Isma'il was Ya'qub's paternal uncle, yet he is called a 'father', showing the term extends to uncles.
The Quranic usage is qat'i in transmission but zanni in implication (dalala).
4
Analyze the hadith proof for maternal uncle
The Prophet said, 'The maternal uncle is a father' (al-khal rab). This hadith, though considered gharib (weak) by some, is accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a basis.
A variant in Musnad al-Firdaws specifies: when the father is not alive, the maternal uncle takes his place.
5
Analyze the rationale for stepfather
Stepfathers are called 'father' due to their role in upbringing (tarbiyah). This is based on common custom ('urf), not a direct scriptural proof.
Custom (urf) is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی کو ماموں، چایا سوتیلے باپ کی طرف منسوب کرنے سے حد کا حکم
وَإِنْ نَسَبَهُ إِلى عَمِهِ أَوْ خَالِهِ أَوْ إِلَى زَوْجِ أَمِهِ فَلَيْسَ بِقَاذِفِ لِاَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ هَؤُلَاءِ يُسَمَّى أَبَا أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَلِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى نَعْبُدُ لَهَكَ وَالَهَ آبَاءِ كَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَقَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ كَانَ عَمَّالَهُ وَالثَّانِي لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْخَالُ رَبِّ وَالثَّالِثُ لِلتَّرْبِيَةِ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے کسی کو اس کے چا یا ماموں یا ماں کے شوہر کی طرف منسوب کیا۔ یعنی اس کو اس کے چایا ماموں یا سوتیلے باپ کا لڑکا بتایا تو وہ تہمت لگانے والا نہیں کہا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان لوگوں میں سے ہر ایک کو باپ بولا جاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اس آیت پاک نعبد الهك والــه ابـائك ابراهیم و اسماعیل و اسحاق میں ہے یعنی حضرت یعقوب و اسماعیل وافق کے پروردگار کی عبادت کریں گے۔ حالانکہ اسماعیل علیہ السلام حضرت یعقوب علیہ السلام کے چاتھے اور ماموں کو باپ کہنا اس دلیل سے ہے کہ حدیث میں مذکور ہے کہ ماموں باپ ہے۔ (لیکن یہ حدیث غریب ہے۔ البتہ مسند الفردوس میں یہ روایت ہے کہ جس کے والد زندہ نہ ہوں تو اس کے ماموں اس کے والد ہیں۔ الزیلعی ) اور سوتیلا باپ تربیت کی بناء پر باپ کہلاتا ہے۔ تشریح ... وان نسبه الى عمه او خاله اوالى زوج امه فليس بقاذف لان كل واحد ... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Ruling on attributing someone to his paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or mother's husband. And if he attributes him to his paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or mother's husband, he is not a slanderer, because each of these is called a father. As for the first, by His saying: 'We worship your God and the God of your fathers Ibrahim and Isma'il and Ishaq' while Isma'il was his (Ya'qub's) paternal uncle. As for the second, by his (the Prophet's) saying: 'The maternal uncle is a father.' And the third, due to upbringing (tarbiyah). Translation: If someone attributes another to his paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or stepfather, he is not a slanderer because each of these is called a father. Evidence: Quranic verse where Isma'il is called a father of Ya'qub though he was his paternal uncle. Hadith: 'The maternal uncle is a father' (though this hadith is considered gharib; a version in Musnad al-Firdaws says when the father is not alive, the maternal uncle is the father). Stepfather is called father due to upbringing. Commentary: 'And if he attributes him to his paternal uncle...' etc., meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This ruling addresses whether attributing someone to a relative other than the biological father could be qadhf. The text says no, because in Islamic usage, paternal uncle ('amm), maternal uncle (khal), and stepfather (zawj al-umm) are all called 'father' (ab) in a broad sense. The Quranic proof: in Surah al-Baqarah, Ibrahim, Isma'il, and Ishaq are called 'fathers' of Ya'qub, though Isma'il was his paternal uncle. The Prophet said 'The maternal uncle is a father' (though the hadith is weak). Stepfather is called father due to his role in upbringing. Therefore, calling someone 'son of your uncle' etc., does not imply an allegation of illegitimacy, so no hadd.

Key Terms
عم (amm): Paternal uncle, often called 'father' in extended sense.
خال (khal): Maternal uncle, can be called 'father' based on hadith.
زوج الأم (zawj al-umm): Stepfather, called 'father' due to upbringing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the Prophet said 'The maternal uncle is a father'.
C) Because the Quran explicitly calls uncles fathers.
D) Because it is a compliment.

Key Takeaway
Attributing someone to a paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or stepfather is not qadhf because Islamic usage broadly considers them as 'father'.

Zanat fil-Jabal: Context vs. Literal Meaning in Qadhf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qadhf with homophone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether saying 'zanat fil-jabal' constitutes qadhf, and explain why context overrides the literal claim of climbing.

Core Idea
Context of insult overrides literal meaning in qadhf; the claim of climbing is not accepted.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the word 'zanat', which can mean either 'climbing' (with hamzah) or 'fornication' (with tashdid). When someone says 'zanat fil-jabal' and claims he meant climbing, does he incur hadd? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say yes; Muhammad says no. The disagreement hinges on whether the context of anger and insult determines the intended meaning or whether the literal sense of climbing is reinforced by mentioning the mountain. This case illustrates the Hanafi principle that contextual evidence (qarinah) can override the literal meaning when the speaker is clearly insulting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its linguistic ambiguity
The act is saying 'zanat fil-jabal' to another person. The word 'zanat' can be interpreted as 'climbing' (with hamzah) or 'fornication' (with tashdid). The speaker claims he meant climbing.
2
State the Hanafi majority position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the claim is not accepted; hadd is wajib because the context of anger and insult specifies fornication as the intended meaning.
The majority view is considered mufta bihi.
3
Understand Imam Muhammad's counterargument
Muhammad argues that the word with hamzah literally means climbing, and the mention of the mountain confirms that meaning; hence no hadd.
He also cites an Arab woman's poetry using 'zina' for climbing.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority respond that the word is also used for fornication even when spelled without hamzah (with softened letter), and the context of insult overrides the literal possibility of climbing. The phrase 'fil-jabal' does not specify climbing as clearly as 'ala al-jabal' would.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority view, hadd is imposed; under Muhammad's view, no hadd. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The practical consequence is that the defendant is subject to hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی کو زناءت في الجبل يازنات علی الجبل یا زانی کہا حد جاری ہوگی یا نہیں
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِغَيْرِهِ زَنَاتَ فِي الْجَبَلِ وَقَالَ عَنَيْتُ صُعُودَ الْجَبَلِ حُدَّ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفٌ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لَا يُحَدُّلَاتَ الْمَهُمُوزَمِنْهُ لِلصُّعُودِ حَقِيقَةٌ قَالَتْ اِمْرَأَةٌ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ ع وَارْقَ إِلَى الْخَيْرَاتِ زِنَاءً فِي الْجَبَلِ وَذِكْرُ الْجَبَلِ يُقَرِّرُهُ مُرَادًا وَلَهُمَا إِنَّهُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِى الْفَاحِشَةِ مَهْمُوزًا أَيْضًالِاَنَّ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ مَنْ يَعْمُرُ الْمُلَيَّنَ كَمَايُلَيَّنُ الْمَهُمُوزُ وَ حَالَةُ الْغَضَبِ وَالسَّبَابِ تَعِيْنُ الْفَاحِشَةِ مُرَاد بمنزلة مَا إِذَا قَالَ يَازَانئِي أَوْقَالَ زَنَاتَ وَذِكْرُ الْجَبَلِ إِنَّمَا يُعَيِّنُ الصُّعُودَ مُرَادًا إِذَا كَانَ مَقْرُونًا بِكَلِمَةِ عَلَى إِذْهُوَ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ فِيْهِ وَلَوْ قَالَ زَنَاتُ عَلَى الْجَبَل قِيْلَ لَا يُحَدُّ لِمَا قَلْنَا وَقِيلَ يُحَدُّ لِلْمَعْنَى الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے سے کہا زنات فی الجبل ۔ پھر یہ دعویٰ کیا کہ اس سے میری مراد یہ تھی کہ تم پہاڑ پر چڑھے تو یہ بات مقبول نہ ہوگی اور اس کہنے پر اسے حد قذف لگائی جائے گی یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ وابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا ہے۔ لیکن امام محمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اسے حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ لفظ زنا جو ہمزہ کے ساتھ ہو وہ حقیقت میں اوپر چڑھائی کرنے کے حق میں آتا ہے۔ اور زنا کاری کے معنی میں مجاز ا
Whether hadd is imposed for saying 'zanat fil-jabal' or 'zanat 'ala al-jabal' or 'zani'. And whoever says to another 'zanat fil-jabal' and says 'I meant climbing the mountain', he is subjected to hadd. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said he is not subjected to hadd because the word with hamzah (zana'a) is literally for climbing. An Arab woman said: 'We aspire to good deeds, climbing the mountain.' And mentioning the mountain confirms that meaning. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it is also used for fornication with hamzah because some Arabs make the softened letter as if it were pronounced with hamzah. And the context of anger and insult determines the meaning of fornication, similar to if he said 'O fornicator' or 'zanat'. And mentioning the mountain would only specify climbing if accompanied by the word 'ala' because that is the common usage. And if he said 'zanat 'ala al-jabal', it is said he is not subjected to hadd for our stated reason, and it is said he is subjected to hadd for the meaning we mentioned. Translation: If someone says to another 'zanat fil-jabal' and claims he meant climbing the mountain, it is not accepted and he is subjected to hadd. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said he is not subjected to hadd because the word with hamzah is literally for climbing. An Arab woman said: 'We aspire to good deeds, climbing the mountain.' And mentioning the mountain supports that. For them, it is also used for fornication with hamzah because some Arabs pronounce it as if with hamzah. The context of anger and insult specifies fornication as intended, similar to if he said 'O fornicator' or 'zanat'. Mentioning the mountain only specifies climbing if accompanied by 'ala', as that is the common usage. If he said 'zanat 'ala al-jabal', some say no hadd, some say hadd.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the word 'zanat' [زَنَاتَ] which can mean either 'he climbed' (with hamzah) or 'he committed fornication' (with tashdid). The issue is whether saying 'zanat fil-jabal' constitutes qadhf when the speaker claims he meant climbing. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the claim is not accepted because the context of anger and insult indicates fornication, and the word is used for fornication even when spelled without hamzah (with softened letter). Imam Muhammad says the word with hamzah literally means climbing, and mentioning the mountain reinforces that; hence no hadd. The text also notes that if the phrase is 'zanat 'ala al-jabal', the claim of climbing is more plausible. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (hadd applies).

Key Terms
زنا (zina): Fornication/adultery; also a homophone for climbing with hamzah.
همزة (hamzah): The glottal stop; distinguishes 'zana'a' (climb) from 'zana' (fornication).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His claim is accepted and no hadd is imposed.
B) Hadd is imposed because the context indicates insult.
C) Only a ta'zir punishment is given.
D) The matter is referred to the judge for interpretation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a word can have two meanings, the context of anger and insult specifies the defamatory meaning, and the claim of innocent intent is not accepted.

Attributing a Child to Uncle or Stepfather Is Not Qadhf
Ruling on attributing a child to relatives other than father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attributing a child to a paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or stepfather, and explain the proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Calling someone 'son of an uncle' does not constitute slander because uncles are called fathers.

The crime of qadhf (false accusation of zina) requires a clear statement imputing adultery. But what if one attributes a person to a relative who is not his biological father, such as 'son of his uncle' or 'son of his stepfather'? The Hanafi school rules that such statements do not incur the hadd punishment, because these relatives can legitimately be called 'father' in a broad sense. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the scriptural proofs behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
First, note the act: stating that a person is the child of his paternal uncle, maternal uncle, or stepfather. The ruling: the speaker is not a slanderer (laysa bi-qadif).
The ruling is clear: no hadd for qadhf.
2
Locate the proofs
The text provides three proofs: Quran 2:133 for the paternal uncle, a hadith for the maternal uncle, and the principle of upbringing for the stepfather.
Each proof establishes that the term 'ab' (father) can apply to these relatives.
3
Analyse the Quranic proof
In Quran 2:133, Prophet Ya'qub mentions 'the God of your fathers Ibrahim, Ismail, and Ishaq'. Ismail was Ya'qub's paternal uncle, yet is called a father. This shows that uncles can be called fathers in a general sense.
The verse's context is not about lineage, but the linguistic usage is key.
4
Analyse the hadith proof
The hadith states 'al-khal ab' (the maternal uncle is a father). Though the exact wording in the source is partially unclear, it is a recognized narration.
This hadith directly indicates that the maternal uncle holds the status of a father for the purpose of naming.
5
Examine the justification for stepfather
The stepfather is called a father due to upbringing (tarbiya), based on the custom and the idea that the foster-father is also considered a father in a metaphorical sense.
This proof is based on 'urf (custom) and the intention of the speaker, not an explicit text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ نَسَبَهُ إِلى عَمِهِ أَوْ خَالِهِ أَوْ إِلَى زَوْجِ أَمِهِ فَلَيْسَ بِقَاذِفِ لِاَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ هَؤُلَاءِ يُسَمَّى أَبَا أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَلِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى نَعْبُدُ إِلَهَكَ وَإِلَهَ آبَائِكَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَقَ وَإِسْمَعِيلُ كَانَ عَمَّهُ وَالثَّانِي لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْخَالُ رَبِّ [؟] وَالثَّالِثُ لِلتَّرْبِيَةِ
And if he attributes him to his paternal uncle, or his maternal uncle, or to his mother's husband, then he is not a slanderer, because each of these is called a father. As for the first, due to His statement: 'We worship your God and the God of your fathers Ibrahim, Ismail, and Ishaq' while Ismail was his paternal uncle. And the second, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The maternal uncle is a father [؟]'. And the third, due to upbringing.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Sunnah. The issue is whether calling a person by a relation other than the biological father (e.g., 'son of uncle', 'son of stepfather') constitutes slander (qadhf) if the person is not actually that person's child. The Hanafi ruling is that it does not make one a slanderer, because these relatives (paternal uncle, maternal uncle, stepfather) are also called 'father' in a valid sense. The proof for the paternal uncle being called father is the Quranic verse (2:133) where the Prophet Ya'qub mentions 'the God of your fathers Ibrahim, Ismail, and Ishaq' — Ismail was Ya'qub's paternal uncle, yet called father. The proof for the maternal uncle is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that the maternal uncle is a father, though the exact wording is unclear in this text. The stepfather is called father due to his role in upbringing (tarbiya). Thus, none of these attributions amount to accusing someone of illegitimate birth.

Key Terms
قاذف (qādhi): One who accuses another of zina (adultery/fornication) without proper evidence, subjecting himself to the hadd punishment.
أب (ab): Father; in this context, it includes paternal and maternal uncles and stepfathers due to kinship or upbringing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone calls a person 'son of his maternal uncle' (يا ابن خاله), does that constitute qadhf (slander) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because it implies the person is not his father's son.
B) Yes, because it is an insult.
C) No, because the maternal uncle is called a father in the hadith.
D) No, because it is not a direct accusation of zina.

Key Takeaway
Attributing a child to an uncle or stepfather is not qadhf because these relatives are considered 'fathers' in the Hanafi legal framework.
