قَالَ وَمَنْ وَطِيَ وَطْأً حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ قَاذِفُهُ لِفَوَاتِ الْعِفَّةِ وَهِيَ شَرْطُ الْإِحْصَانِ وَلِأَنَّ الْقَاذِفَ صَادِقٌ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ مَنْ وَطِيَ وَطْأً حَرَامًا لِعَيْنِهِ لَا يَجِبُ الْحَدُّ بِقَذْفِهِ لِأَنَّ الزِّنَا هُوَ الْوَطْءُ الْمُحَرَّمُ لِعَيْنِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُحَرَّمًا لِغَيْرِهِ يُحَدُّ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِزِنَا فَالْوَطْءُ فِي غَيْرِ الْمِلْكِ مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهٍ أَوْ مِنْ وَجْهٍ حَرَامٌ لِعَيْنِهِ وَكَذَا الْوَطْءُ فِي الْمِلْكِ وَالْحُرْمَةُ مُؤَيَّدَةٌ فَإِنْ كَانَتِ الْحُرْمَةُ مُوَقَّتَةً فَالْحُرْمَةُ لِغَيْرِهِ وَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ يَشْتَرِطُ أَنْ تَكُونَ الْحُرْمَةُ الْمُؤَيَّدَةُ ثَابِتَةً بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَوْ بِالْحَدِيثِ الْمَشْهُورِ لِتَكُونَ ثَابِتَةً مِنْ غَيْرِ تَرَدُّدٍ بَيَانُهُ أَنَّ مَنْ قَذَفَ رَجُلًا وَطِيَ جَارِيَةٍ مُشْتَرَكَةٍ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخَرَ فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ لِانْعِدَامِ الْمِلْكِ مِنْ وَجْهٍ
He said: And whoever performs intercourse that is forbidden while not in his ownership, his slanderer is not punished with hadd, because of the loss of chastity which is a condition of ihsan, and because the slanderer is truthful. The principle in this is that whoever performs intercourse that is forbidden inherently (haram li-'aynihi), the hadd is not required for slandering him, because zinā is intercourse that is inherently forbidden. And if it is forbidden due to something else (li-ghayrihi), he is punished with hadd, because it is not zinā. So intercourse outside ownership, either in all respects or in some respect, is inherently forbidden. Likewise, intercourse within ownership while the prohibition is permanent is inherently forbidden. If the prohibition is temporary, then the prohibition is due to something else. And Abu Hanifa stipulates that the permanent prohibition must be established by consensus (ijmā') or by a well-known hadith, so that it is established without doubt. Its explanation: whoever slanders a man who had intercourse with a slave-girl jointly owned between him and another, then there is no hadd upon him, because of the absence of ownership in some respect.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) by al-Marghinani, explaining a key principle from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of prohibited intercourse on the punishment for slander. The ruling: if a person engages in sexually intercourse that is inherently forbidden (haram li-'aynihi), then slandering that person (calling him a zānī) does not incur hadd al-qadhf. The reason is that such a person has already lost his 'iffah (chastity), which is a condition for ihsan (the protective status requiring hadd for false accusation). Moreover, the slanderer is considered truthful because the person did commit an act that is basically zinā. In contrast, if the intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor (haram li-ghayrihi), such as intercourse during menstruation (which is prohibited but not inherently act of zinā), then slandering that person does incur hadd, because the act is not considered actual zinā, and the person's 'iffah remains intact. The passage then explains the application: intercourse outside ownership in any way (e.g., fornication, or with a slave-girl not fully owned) is inherently forbidden. Also, intercourse within ownership (e.g., with one's own wife or slave-girl) with a permanent prohibition (e.g., due to marriage to a close relative, or a woman who is haram forever, like one's foster mother) is also inherently forbidden. Temporary prohibitions (e.g., during menses, fasting, iḥrām) are classified as haram li-ghayrihi. Imam Abu Hanifa adds a condition: for permanent prohibition to count as inherent, it must be established by ijmā' or mashhūr hadith, ensuring certainty. The example given: a man who has intercourse with a jointly-owned slave-girl (where he shares ownership with another) – if he is slandered as a zānī, the slanderer is not punished because the intercourse took place in a context of partial ownership, which makes it inherently forbidden (since complete milk is absent). This illustrates the principle's application.

Key Terms
الوطء الحرام لعينه (al-waṭ' al-ḥarām li-'aynihi): Sexual intercourse that is unlawful due to its intrinsic nature, such as fornication or intercourse with a non-mahram without valid marriage or ownership.
الوطء الحرام لغيره (al-waṭ' al-ḥarām li-ghayrihi): Sexual intercourse that is unlawful due to an external factor, not because of the act itself. Examples include intercourse during menstruation, fasting, or iḥrām.
ملك (milk): Ownership or legal right to enjoy a woman sexually, either through marriage (milk al-nikāḥ) or through slave ownership (milk al-yamīn).
حديث مشهور (ḥadīth mashhūr): A well-known hadith, transmitted by at least three companions in each generation, which is less than tawātur but strong. Used by Abu Hanifa as a requirement for establishing permanent prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man has intercourse with a slave-girl he owns jointly with his brother. Someone calls him a zānī. What is the ruling on the slanderer according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must receive 80 lashes.
B) No hadd because the intercourse is inherently forbidden due to lack of full ownership.
C) He receives a discretionary punishment.
D) He must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between inherently and externally prohibited intercourse determines whether slander incurs hadd: only inherently forbidden acts (zinā) remove 'iffah and exempt the slanderer from punishment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
12 min
Types of Prohibited Intercourse and Their Effect on Hadd al-Qadhf
Ruling with proof on types of prohibited intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haram 'ayn and haram ghayr and state the ruling on hadd al-qadhf for each case, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on mukataba.

Core Idea
Only inherently prohibited intercourse (haram 'ayn) removes ihsan; temporary prohibitions preserve it, so the accuser receives hadd.

This lesson tackles a subtle but critical distinction in Hanafi criminal law: not all prohibited intercourse is treated equally when it comes to the penalty for false accusation (qadhf). The key is whether the prohibition is inherent to the act (like zina) or merely temporary (like intercourse during menstruation). Understanding this distinction determines whether the accuser is punished or not, and it hinges on the condition of ihsan (chastity). We will walk through the principles, specific cases, and a famous internal Hanafi disagreement over the mukataba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
The text divides prohibited intercourse into two categories: haram 'ayn (inherently prohibited, essentially zina) and haram ghayr (externally prohibited, temporary). Recognize that the first category removes the attribute of chastity ('iffa) from the accused, while the second does not.
Haram 'ayn includes intercourse outside ownership, with a permanently prohibited woman, etc. Haram ghayr includes menstruation, ihram, or with a mukataba.
2
Apply the distinction to hadd al-qadhf
If the accused committed haram 'ayn, he is no longer muhsin; thus, the accuser is truthful and not liable for hadd. If the accused committed haram ghayr, he remains muhsin, so the accuser is liable for 80 lashes.
The condition for hadd al-qadhf is that the accused must be muhsin (free, Muslim, adult, sane, chaste).
3
Examine the specific cases
The text lists several cases: shared slave-girl (partially owned → haram 'ayn, no hadd on accuser); woman who committed zina while Christian (zina confirmed, no hadd); intercourse with one's own Majusiyya slave-girl, menstruating wife, or mukataba (ownership intact, prohibition temporary → hadd on accuser).
The case of the mukataba involves an intra-Hanafi dispute, which we will analyze.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on mukataba
Abu Yusuf and Zufar argue that intercourse with a mukataba removes ihsan because ownership for intercourse is suspended (as evidenced by the 'uqr compensation). The majority (Abu Hanifa) hold that milk al-dhat remains, so the prohibition is temporary and ihsan is preserved.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Derive the ruling for a new case
Apply the principle to a hypothetical: if a man has intercourse with his wife during her postpartum bleeding (nifas), is the accuser punished? Since the prohibition is temporary and ownership remains, the wife is still muhsina, so the accuser must receive hadd.
This confirms the pattern: temporary prohibitions do not break ihsan.

باب حد القذف
وَطَيَ جَارِيَةٍ مُشْتَرَكَةٍ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخَرَ فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ لِانْعِدَامِ الْمِلْكِ مِنْ وَجْهٍ
ترجمہ: جس نے اپنے غیر ملک میں حرام وطی کی تو اس پر تہمت لگانے والے کسی کو حد نہیں لگائی جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی پاکدامنی ختم ہو گئی۔ حالانکہ احصان کی شرط پاکدامن اور عفیفہ ہوتا ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ اس صورت میں الزام لگانے والا سچا ہے۔ اس باب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ جس نے کوئی ایسی وطی کی جو اپنی ذات سے حرام ہو تو اس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ زنا ایسی ہی وطی کو کہتے ہیں جو اپنی ذات میں حرام ہو تو اس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ حقیقت میں یہ زنا نہیں ہے اب اگر کسی ایسی عورت سے وطی کی جو کسی بھی وجہ سے یا کسی ایک وجہ سے ملک میں نہیں ہے وہ اپنی ذات سے حرام ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر ملک نکاح یا ملک رقبہ موجود ہونے کے ساتھ وطی کی۔ لیکن یہ عورت اس پر ہمیشہ کے لئے حرام ہو تو بھی یہ اپنی ذات سے حرام ہوگی اور اگر وطی کا حرام ہونا کسی مخصوص وقت کے لئے ہو جیسے حیض کی حالت میں وطی حرام ہوتی ہے۔ تو یہ حرمت کسی خارجی وجہ سے ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ ابدی حرمت میں یہ شرط لگاتے ہیں کہ اس کا ثبوت اجماع یا کسی مشہور حدیث سے ہوتا کہ کسی تردد کے بغیر اس کا ثبوت ہو۔ اس اصل کے مسائل آئندہ بیان کئے ہیں۔ جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ کہ جس نے ایسی کسی باندی سے وطی کی جو اس نے اور دوسرے کے درمیان مشترک تھی۔ پس کسی نے اس کو زانی کہا تو اس کی وجہ سے اسے حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ ایک اعتبار سے ملکیت میں نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: قَالَ وَمَنْ وَطِيَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ قَاذِفُهُ لِفَوَاتِ الْعِفَّةِ ... الخ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مملوکہ عورت سے حرام وطی کی اور اس پر کسی نے زنا کی تہمت لگائی تو اس صورت میں حد جاری نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مقذوف میں ( وطی حرام کا مرتکب ) صفت عفت نہیں پائی جاتی جو کہ احصان کے لئے مشروط ہے۔ غرض حرمت وطی کے وجود کے باعث مقذوف ( زنا کی تہمت یافتہ) کی صفت عفیف (پاکدامن) کے فقدان کی بنا پر قاذف پر حد قذف جاری نہ ہوگی۔ بایں وجہ کہ قاذف پر حد قذف کی اقامت کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ مقذوف میں قذف کے احصان کی پانچوں شرائط پائی جائیں۔ لیکن مقذوف نے جب وطی حرام کا ارتکاب کر لیا تو اس سے صفت عفت زائل ہوگی۔ لہذا اگر کسی نے وطی حرام کے مرتکب پر قذف (زنا کی تہمت) کیا تو مقذوف کے محصن و عفیف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس ( قاذف) پر حد قذف جاری نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مقذوف کے محصن نہ ہونے کی صورت میں قاذف کا قول مبنی بر صدق ہوتا ہے۔ مذکورہ صورت کے زیر بحث مسئلہ میں اصل یہ ہے کہ جس نے ایسی وطی کی جس کی حرمت عینہ ہے تو اس کے قذف پر حد واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حرام عینہ در اصل خالص زنا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زانی یا زانیہ پر تہمت لگانا موجب حد نہیں۔
جانا چاہئے کہ اصل کے اعتبار سے وطی حرام دو قسم ہے۔ ا۔ وطی حرام عینہ ایسی وطی جس کی حرمت ذاتی طور پر موجود ہو۔ جیسے ایسی عورت سے وطی کرنا جو بالکل غیر مملوکہ ہو یا بالواسطہ غیر مملوکہ ہو یا ملک نکاح و ملک رقبہ کے پائے جانے پر وطی کی جائے۔ جب کہ وہ عورت ابدی حرمت کی حامل ہو تو اس صورت میں وطی حرام عینہ قرار پائے گی۔ جو کہ در حقیقت زنا ہے۔ لہذا اس (وطی حرام عینہ) کا قذف موجب حد نہ ہوگا۔ وطی حرام غیر وہ وطی جو اپنی ذات میں کسی امر خارجی کے باعث حرام ہو۔ جیسا کہ حالت حیض و نفاس وغیرہ کی وجہ سے حرمت وقتی تو اس صورت میں وطی حرام لغیرہ قرار پائے گی۔ جو کہ دراصل زنا نہیں ہے۔ لہذا صفت احصان کے عدم سقوط کی بناء پر اس ( وطی حرام لغیرہ) کا قذف موجب ہوگا۔ اگر کسی شخص نے ایسی لونڈی خریدی جس سے خریدار کا باپ وطی کر چکا ہے یا خریدار اپنی ماں کی لونڈی سے وطی کر چکا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں خریدار نے اس لونڈی سے وطی (ہمبستری) کی پھر کسی دوسرے شخص نے اسے (خریدار کو ) قذف کیا تو اس صورت میں بالا جماع قاذف پر حد جاری نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ وطی حرام لغیرہ کے زمرے میں ہے۔ لیکن امام ابوحنیفہ ابدی حرمت میں شرط لازمی قرار دیتے ہیں۔ کہ اس (ابدی حرمت) کا تحقق ( ثبوت ) اجماع امت یا حدیث مشہورہ سے تحقق ( ثابت ) ہو۔ تا کہ اس ( ابدی حرمت) کے تحقیق میں کسی قسم کا تردد نہ پایا جائے ۔ جیسا کہ مذکورہ صورت ( خریدار کی وہ لونڈی جس سے اس کا باپ وطی کر چکا یا خریدار نے اپنی ماں کی لونڈی سے وطی کی) کی ابدی حرمت بالا جماع ثابت ہے یا ابدی حرمت حدیث مشہورہ سے ثابت ہو ۔ جیسا کہ حدیث میں مذکور ہے ” لا نکاح الا بشهود ( گواہوں کے بغیر نکاح نہیں) چنانچہ اس حدیث کی رو سے بلا تردد ابدی حرمت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے یعنی کسی آدمی نے ایسی عورت سے نکاح کیا جو اس پر ابدی حرام ہے۔ چنانچہ اس سے وطی کرنے کی صورت میں احصان ساقط ہو گیا لہذا قاذف کے لئے یہ صورت موجب حد نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے بقول ابدی حرمت میں بالا جماع یا حدیث مشہورہ پر مبنی بلا تردد ثبوت کی (اصل پر مشتمل مسائل) کے بیان میں ) یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایسی لونڈی سے وطی کی جو اس اور غیر کے درمیان باہم مشترک ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے مشترکہ لونڈی سے وطی (ہمبستری) کرنے والے کو قذف کرتے ہوئے اسے "زانی" کہا تو اس پر حد قذف واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ بوجہ اشتراک ایک طرف سے وہ (لونڈی ) اس (واطی ) کی بھی غیر مملوکہ ہے بایں وجہ کہ اس ( موطوہ لونڈی) میں غیر کی ملکیت بھی موجود ہے۔
وَ كَذَا إِذَا قَذَفَ امْرَأَةً زَنَتْ فِي نَصْرَانِيَّتِهَا لِتَحَقُّقِ الزِّنَاءِ مِنْهَا شَرْعًا لِانْعِدَامِ الْمِلْكِ وَلِهَذَا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَدُّ وَلَوْ قَذَفَ رَجُلًا أَتَى أَمَتَهُ وَهِيَ مَجُوسِيَّةٌ أَوِ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ أَوْ مُكَاتَبَةً لَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لِأَنَّ الْحُرْمَةَ مَعَ قِيَامِ الْمِلْكِ وَهِيَ مُوَقَّتَةٌ فَكَانَ الْحُرْمَةُ لِغَيْرِهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ زِنَاءً وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ وَطْءَ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ يُسْقِطُ الْإِحْصَانَ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ لِأَنَّ الْمِلْكَ زَائِلٌ فِي حَقِّ الْوَطْءِ وَلِهَذَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْعُقْرُ بِالْوَطْءِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ مِلْكُ الذَّاتِ بَاقٍ وَالْحُرْمَةُ بِغَيْرِهِ إِذْ هِيَ مُوَقَّتَةٌ
Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. He had intercourse with a slave-girl shared between him and another, so there is no hadd upon him due to the absence of ownership from one aspect. Translation: Whoever commits prohibited intercourse outside his ownership, then the one who accuses him is not subject to hadd, because his chastity is lost. Although the condition of ihsan is to be chaste and virtuous, and also because in this case the accuser is truthful. The principle in this chapter is that whoever commits intercourse that is inherently prohibited, the one who accuses him will not be punished with hadd. Because zina is called such an intercourse which is inherently prohibited, so the accuser will be punished with hadd (only if the act is not inherently prohibited). Because in reality this is not zina. Now if he has intercourse with a woman who for any reason or for one reason is not in his ownership, she will be inherently prohibited. Similarly, if he has intercourse despite the existence of marriage ownership or slave ownership, but this woman is permanently prohibited to him, then it is inherently prohibited. And if the prohibition of intercourse is for a specific time, like intercourse during menstruation is prohibited, then this prohibition is due to an external cause. Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) stipulates in eternal prohibition that its proof must be by consensus or a well-known hadith, without any doubt. The issues of this principle are explained later. Its detail is: Whoever had intercourse with a slave-girl who was shared between him and another, then someone called him a fornicator, so due to that he will not be punished with hadd, because from one aspect she is not in his ownership. Commentary: He said: And whoever commits an act of intercourse that is prohibited and outside his ownership, his accuser is not punished with hadd due to the loss of chastity... etc. The situation is that if someone had prohibited intercourse with a woman not owned by him, and someone accused him of zina, then in this case hadd will not be carried out. Because the accused (the one who committed prohibited intercourse) does not possess the attribute of chastity, which is a condition for ihsan. In short, due to the existence of prohibited intercourse, the accused's attribute of chastity is lost, so the accuser will not be punished with hadd al-qadhf. Because for the execution of hadd on the accuser, it is a condition that the accused possesses all five conditions of ihsan. But when the accused committed prohibited intercourse, the attribute of chastity is removed. Therefore, if someone makes an accusation (of zina) against the perpetrator of prohibited intercourse, due to the accused not being muhsin and chaste, the hadd will not be carried out on the accuser, because in the case of the accused not being muhsin, the accuser's statement is based on truth. In the discussed situation, the principle is that whoever commits intercourse whose prohibition is intrinsic ('ayn), then his accusation does not necessitate hadd. Because intrinsic prohibition is in reality pure zina. From this it is understood that accusing a fornicator or adulteress does not cause hadd. It should be known that according to the principle, prohibited intercourse is of two types: 1. Haram 'ayn: intercourse whose prohibition is intrinsically present, like having intercourse with a woman who is absolutely not owned, or indirectly not owned, or despite the existence of marriage ownership or slave ownership, when that woman has eternal prohibition. In this case, it is considered haram 'ayn, which is actually zina. Therefore, the accusation of such (haram 'ayn) does not cause hadd. 2. Haram ghayr: intercourse that is prohibited due to an external matter, like prohibition of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, etc. Then this is temporary prohibition, so it is considered haram li ghayrihi, which in reality is not zina. Therefore, due to the non-removal of the attribute of ihsan, the accusation of such (haram li ghayrihi) will cause hadd. If a person bought a slave-girl with whom the buyer's father had intercourse, or the buyer had intercourse with his mother's slave-girl, then in both cases the buyer had intercourse with that slave-girl. Then another person accused him (the buyer) with qadhf. In this case, by consensus, the accuser will not be punished with hadd, because this is in the category of haram li ghayrihi. But Imam Abu Hanifa makes a condition in eternal prohibition that its confirmation must be by consensus of the ummah or a well-known hadith, so that there is no doubt in its verification. Just as in the mentioned case (the buyer's slave-girl with whom his father had intercourse, or the buyer had intercourse with his mother's slave-girl) the eternal prohibition is established by consensus, or eternal prohibition is established by a well-known hadith. As mentioned in the hadith: 'There is no marriage except with witnesses' (La nikaha illa bi shuhud). According to this hadith, without doubt, eternal prohibition is established. That is, if a man married a woman who is eternally prohibited to him, then having intercourse with her results in the loss of ihsan, so this case does not cause hadd for the accuser. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in eternal prohibition based on consensus or well-known hadith without doubt (the issues based on this principle) are: A person had intercourse with a slave-girl who is shared between him and another. If someone accuses the one who had intercourse with the shared slave-girl, calling him a 'fornicator', then hadd al-qadhf is not obligatory on him, because due to the sharing, from one aspect the slave-girl is not owned by him (the one who had intercourse), because the ownership of the other (partner) also exists in her. Similarly, if he accused a woman who committed zina during her Christianity, because zina is confirmed from her legally due to the absence of ownership, and for this reason hadd was obligatory upon her. And if he accused a man who had intercourse with his female slave while she was a Zoroastrian, or his wife while she was menstruating, or his mukataba, then hadd is upon him (the accuser) because the prohibition exists despite the ownership being established, and it is temporary, so the prohibition is due to something else, and thus it was not zina. And from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it is narrated that intercourse with a mukataba removes ihsan, and this is the saying of Zufar, because ownership is non-existent in terms of intercourse, and for this reason the 'uqr (compensation for loss of virginity) becomes due upon him by intercourse. And we say: ownership of the essence (milk al-dhat) remains, and the prohibition is due to something else, since it is temporary.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of hadd al-qadhf. It explains the legal distinction between types of prohibited intercourse and their effect on the punishment for false accusation (qadhf). The key principle is that if the accused person has committed an act of intercourse that is inherently prohibited (haram 'ayn) – i.e., it is zina in essence – then the accuser is not punished with hadd because the accused has lost the attribute of chastity ('iffa), which is a condition for ihsan (being muhsin). However, if the prohibition is temporary or external (haram li ghayrihi), such as intercourse during menstruation or with a mukataba, then the act is not considered zina, and the accuser is punished with hadd unless the accused has lost ihsan through another cause. The text then details specific cases: a shared slave-girl (ownership is partial, so the act is partially zina, and the accuser is not punished); a woman who committed zina while a Christian (the zina is established, so the accuser is not punished); and cases where a man has intercourse with his own property: a Majusiyya slave-girl, his menstruating wife, or his mukataba. In these, the accuser is punished because the prohibition is temporary and ownership remains. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Zufar hold that intercourse with a mukataba removes ihsan because the right to intercourse is suspended (ownership for intercourse is absent), as evidenced by the obligation of 'uqr. The majority (including Abu Hanifa) argue that the essence of ownership (milk al-dhat) remains, and the prohibition is temporary, so ihsan is not lost. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the majority.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (adultery/fornication) against a muhsin person.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being chaste and free (free Muslim, adult, sane, and never committed zina).
حرام عين (haram 'ayn): Prohibition that is inherent to the act itself, not due to an external factor.
حرام غير (haram ghayr): Prohibition due to a temporary or external factor, such as menstruation or ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa), does intercourse with one's mukataba (a slave-girl who has a contract of emancipation) remove the condition of ihsan (chastity)?
A) Yes, because the right to intercourse is suspended.
B) No, because the ownership of her person remains and the prohibition is temporary.
C) Yes, because he must pay 'uqr (compensation).
D) No, because the mukataba is not his property at all.

Key Takeaway
The key to hadd al-qadhf is whether the accused has lost ihsan through inherently prohibited intercourse (haram 'ayn); temporary prohibitions do not break ihsan, and thus the accuser is punished.

Qadhf of a Woman Who Committed Zina During Kufr
Ruling on qadhf against a woman who committed zina during kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qadhf when the accused woman actually committed zina during her kufr and explain the reason (talil) based on Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
If the zina actually occurred, the accusation is true and no hadd for qadhf applies.

The hadd for qadhf (false accusation of zina) protects the honour of the innocent. But what if the woman indeed committed zina? In that case, the accusation is truthful, and the hadd is lifted. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a specific scenario: a woman who committed zina while a Christian (before Islam) is later accused. The ruling clarifies that the accuser is not liable for hadd because the zina is legally confirmed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is qadhf (accusing a woman of zina). The ruling is that the accuser is not subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes).
2
Locate the reason (talil)
The reason given is 'li-tahaqquq al-zina' (because the zina is confirmed) and 'li-in'idam al-milk' (due to absence of ownership, meaning she was not the accuser's slave, so her act was indeed zina).
The confirmation of zina makes the accusation true.
3
Understand the condition of the accused
The woman committed zina during her kufr (Christianity). This establishes that the act occurred, even if she later embraced Islam. The hadd for zina would be obligatory upon her, but that is separate.
The faith status at the time of zina is irrelevant for confirming the act.
4
Apply the principle
Qadhf hadd is only for false accusations. Since the accusation is true, no hadd. The same would apply if the zina occurred before or after marriage, as long as it is confirmed.
This is a straightforward application of the principle that truthfulness negates the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ كَذَا إِذَا قَذَفَ امْرَاةٌ زَنَتْ فِي نَصْرَانِيَّتِهَا لِتَحَقَّقِ الزِّنَاءِ مِنْهَا شَرْعًا لِإِنْعِدَامِ الْمِلْكِ وَلِهَذَا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَدُّ
Similarly, if he accuses a woman who committed zina in her Christianity, because the zina is legally confirmed from her due to absence of ownership, and therefore the hadd is obligatory upon her.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on qadhf (false accusation of zina). The passage states that if a person accuses a woman of zina who actually committed zina while she was a Christian (before Islam), then the accuser is not subject to the hadd punishment for qadhf. The reason is that the zina is legally established against her, so the accusation is true. The phrase 'absence of ownership' indicates that she was not the slave of the accused, so her act was indeed zina. Consequently, she herself is liable for the hadd of zina. The ruling is based on the principle that qadhf hadd is only for accusing an innocent person of zina; if the act occurred, the accusation is veracious.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina or adultery
نصرانية (nasrāniyya): Christianity or the state of being Christian
زناء (zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim accuses a woman of zina who had committed zina while she was a Christian, what is the ruling on the accuser?
A) The accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf
B) The accuser is not subject to any hadd because the zina is confirmed
C) The accuser must pay a fine
D) The accuser is given a discretionary punishment

Key Takeaway
Truthful accusation of zina, when the zina is confirmed, does not incur the hadd of qadhf.

Accusing a Man for Intercourse with His Own Temporarily Prohibited Property
Ruling on qadhf against a man who had intercourse with his own property with a temporary prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qadhf when the accused had intercourse with his own slave, menstruating wife, or mukatabah, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect on ihsan.

Core Idea
Intercourse with one’s own property is not zina if the prohibition is temporary — the accuser gets hadd.

This passage examines a nuanced area of hudud law: what happens when a man is accused of zina for having intercourse with a woman he owns, but where intercourse is temporarily prohibited? The Hanafi school rules that such intercourse is not zina because ownership remains, so the accuser is liable for qadhf. The passage also addresses a disagreement among Hanafi imams about whether intercourse with a mukatabah nullifies ihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the cases: (1) own Magian slave woman, (2) wife during menstruation, (3) own mukatabah. Each involves a prohibited act but the woman is owned (or like-owned in marriage).
The prohibition is temporary in each case.
2
Extract the underlying principle
The text states 'al-hurmah ma'a qiyam al-milk, wa hiya muwaqqatah' — the prohibition coexists with ownership and is temporary. Therefore, the act is not zina.
Ownership of the essence (milk al-dhat) remains.
3
Apply the ruling to the accuser
Since the act is not zina, an accusation of zina is false, and the accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). This is wajib.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Zufar argue that intercourse with a mukatabah nullifies ihsan because ownership is partially removed (evidenced by the liability for 'uqr). Abu Hanifa holds that milk al-dhat remains, so ihsan is not nullified.
The dispute is specific to the mukatabah case.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If ihsan were nullified, the man would no longer be muhsan, and a future zina would carry a lighter hadd (100 lashes instead of stoning). In this context, the accuser still gets hadd regardless, but the ruling on ihsan affects other scenarios.
The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَدَقَ رَجُلًا أتي امته وَهِيَ مَجُوسِيَّةٌ أو امْرَأَتُهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ اَوْ مُكَاتَبَةٌ لَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّلَاتَ الْحُرْمَةَ مَعَ قِيَامِ الْمِلْكِ وَهِيَ مُوَفَّتَةٌ فَكَانَ الحرمة لِغَيْرِهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ زِنَاءً وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفٌ اَنَّ وَطَيَ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ يُسْقِطُ الْإِحْصَانَ وَهُوَقَوْلُ زُفَرٌ لِاَنَّ الْمِلْكَ زَائِلٌ فِي حَقِ الْوَطيِ وَلِهَذَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْعُقْرُ بِالْوَلِّي وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ مِلْكُ الدَّاتِ بَاقِ وَالْحُرْمَةُ بِغَيْرِهِ إِذْهِيَ مُوَفَّتَةٌ
And if he accuses a man who had intercourse with his slave woman while she is a Magian, or his wife while she is menstruating, or his mukatabah, then the hadd is upon him (the accuser) because the prohibition is with the existence of ownership, and it is temporary, so the prohibition is due to something external, so it is not zina. And from Abu Yusuf: that intercourse with the mukatabah nullifies ihsan, and this is the saying of Zufar, because ownership is removed in respect to intercourse, and therefore he owes the 'uqr for the intercourse. And we say: the ownership of the essence remains, and the prohibition is due to something else, since it is temporary.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage covers three scenarios where a man has intercourse with a woman who is his property but temporarily prohibited: (1) his own Magian slave woman (intercourse with her is prohibited due to her faith, but she is still his property), (2) his wife during menstruation (intercourse is haram due to impurity, but she is his wife), (3) his mukatabah (a slave woman who has made a contract of manumission and is partially free, so intercourse is prohibited during the contract). In all these cases, the act is not zina because the woman is owned by the man (in case of wife, she is his wife, which is like ownership in this context). The prohibition is temporary and external, so the act does not constitute zina. Therefore, if someone falsely accuses such a man of zina, the accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). There is a disagreement regarding the mukatabah: Abu Yusuf and Zufar hold that intercourse with a mukatabah nullifies ihsan (the state of being muhsan required for the stricter hadd for zina) because ownership is partially removed; they also note that the man must pay 'uqr (compensation) for the intercourse. However, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon view) is that core ownership remains, so ihsan is not nullified, and the prohibition is external, hence the act is not zina.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukātaba): A female slave who has entered into a kitabah (contract of manumission) and is partially free
إحصان (iḥṣān): The state of being muhsan (free, adult, Muslim, and having had valid marital intercourse) which makes the hadd for zina stoning instead of lashes
عقر (ʿuqr): Compensation paid for the loss of virginity or for unlawful intercourse with a slave woman

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone accuses a man of zina for having intercourse with his own Magian slave woman, what is the ruling?
A) The accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf
B) The accuser is not subject to any hadd because the act is zina
C) The accuser receives a discretionary punishment
D) The accused is subject to hadd for zina

Key Takeaway
Intercourse with one's own property or wife under a temporary prohibition is not zina; thus false accusation triggers the hadd of qadhf.

Qadhf and the Foster-Sister Slave Woman
Ruling on qadhf when the accused committed zina with a foster-sister slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the accuser when the accused committed zina with a woman who is eternally prohibited due to fosterage, and explain why no hadd applies.

Core Idea
An accusation of zina is not punished if the act actually was zina—even with one's own slave if she is a foster-relative.

This lesson examines a specific scenario under the law of qadhf (false accusation of zina). The general rule is that accusing a chaste person of zina incurs the hadd punishment. However, if the accused actually committed zina, the accusation is true and the accuser is not punished. Here, a man is accused of having intercourse with his own slave woman who is his foster-sister. Because foster-sibling creates an eternal prohibition (hurma mu'abbada), the act constitutes zina. Therefore, the accusation is true and no hadd is imposed on the accuser.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is qadhf (accusing a man of zina). The ruling in this case is that the accuser is not subject to the hadd of qadhf.
The hadd of qadhf applies only when the accusation is false.
2
Analyze the reason (ta'lil)
The text states the ruling is because 'the prohibition is eternal.' This means the woman is eternally forbidden to the man due to the foster relationship, making the intercourse zina. Hence, the accusation is true.
Eternal prohibition (hurma mu'abbada) is established through fosterage (rida') that creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood relation.
3
Apply the principle to the hadd condition
One condition for the hadd of qadhf is that the accusation must be false. Since the accusation here is true, the condition is not met and no hadd is imposed.
This aligns with the Hanafi position that the hadd of qadhf is for protecting honor; truthful accusations do not harm honor.
4
Confirm the authoritative view
The text concludes 'this is the correct,' indicating this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
Some earlier views may have differed, but the school settled on no hadd in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَذَفَ رَجُلًا وَطِيَ آمَتَهُ وَهِيَ أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ لَا يُحَدُّلَانَّ الْحُرْمَةَ مُؤَبَّدَةٌ وَهَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
And if he accuses a man who had intercourse with his slave woman while she is his foster-sister (through breastfeeding), he is not hadded because the prohibition is eternal, and this is the correct.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This ruling addresses the case where a man has intercourse with his own slave woman who is his foster-sister (i.e., he was breastfed by the same woman who owned this slave, so she is his sister by fosterage). Since foster-sibling relationship creates an eternal prohibition (hurma mu'abbada), that woman is forever forbidden to him even though she is his slave. Therefore, intercourse with her is essentially zina. If someone accuses him of zina, the accusation is true, so the accuser is not subject to the hadd of qadhf. The text states 'this is the correct', indicating that this is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رضاع (riḍāʿ): Fosterage or breastfeeding relationship that creates kinship prohibitions
حرمة مؤبدة (ḥurma muʾabbada): Eternal prohibition, never becoming permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the accuser did not use explicit words of accusation.
C) Because the prohibition between the man and his slave woman is eternal, making the act zina.
D) Because the accuser was a close relative of the accused.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf is not imposed when the accusation is true; here, the eternal prohibition from fosterage makes the act zina, so the accuser escapes punishment.

Accusing a Mukatib Who Died Leaving Wealth to Pay Kitabah
Ruling on qadhf against a deceased mukatib whose estate covers the kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qadhf against a deceased mukatib whose estate covers the kitabah and explain why the hadd is averted due to shubha.

Core Idea
When a mukatib dies with sufficient wealth, doubt about his free status repels the hadd of qadhf.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of qadhf (false accusation of zina). The ruling addresses a unique situation where the accused is a mukatib who has died leaving enough property to complete his kitabah. The key legal principle is that hadd punishments are averted by doubts (shubha).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qadhf (accusing someone of zina without proof). The ruling is there is no hadd (fixed punishment) on the accuser. This is the explicit ruling in the text.
2
Understand the status of the accused
The accused is a mukatib (a slave under contract to earn freedom by paying installments). He died leaving enough wealth (wafa') to fulfill the kitabah.
This creates a legal ambiguity: was he free at death or still a slave?
3
Identify the source of doubt (shubha)
The Companions (Sahaba) disagreed on a mukatib's status when he dies with sufficient wealth. Some considered him free from the moment of death; others maintained his slavery until the contract is fully discharged. This ikhtilaf generates a shubha about his free status at the time of the alleged zina.
Ikhtilaf al-Sahaba is a recognized source of shubha in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
The general rule: Hudud penalties are averted by shubha (legal doubts). Because of the shubha in the mukatib's freedom, the hadd of qadhf is not applied to the accuser.
This is a causal reasoning (ta'lil): the presence of shubha blocks the application of hadd.
5
Note the practical consequence
The accuser is not liable for the fixed punishment (80 lashes). However, he may still be subject to ta'zir (discretionary punishment) if the judge deems necessary.
The text only negates the hadd, not any other accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَدَقَ مُكَاتِبًا وَمَاتَ وَتَرَكَ وَفَاءً لَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ لِتَمَكُنِ الشَّبْهَةِ فِى الْحُرِّيَّةِ لِمَكَانَ إِخْتَلَافِ الصَّحَابَةِ
And if he accuses a mukatib and he died leaving sufficient (wealth to pay the kitabah), there is no hadd upon him because of the prevalence of doubt regarding his freedom due to the disagreement of the Companions.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This ruling deals with a mukatib (a slave under a kitabah contract) who died leaving enough property to fulfill the kitabah payment. In such a case, there is ambiguity (shubha) about whether he was actually free at the time of his death, because the Companions (Sahaba) had differing opinions on the status of a mukatib who dies with sufficient wealth. Some considered him free from the moment of death, others maintained his slavery. Due to this legitimate difference of opinion, the accusation of zina against him (if he committed any act) is not punished with hadd for qadhf, as the doubt prevents the hadd from being applied. This follows the Hanafi principle that hadd punishments are repelled by doubt (shubha).

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A male slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to earn his freedom by paying installments
شبهة (shubha): Legal ambiguity or doubt that can avert hadd punishments
اختلاف الصحابة (ikhtilāf al-ṣaḥāba): Disagreement among the Companions of the Prophet on a legal issue, which creates shubha

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone accuses a deceased mukatib of zina, and the mukatib left enough wealth to pay the kitabah, what is the ruling on the accuser?
A) The accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf
B) The accuser is not subject to any hadd because of doubt about freedom
C) The accuser is given a discretionary punishment
D) The hadd is waived only if the mukatib had actually completed the kitabah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule that hudud are averted by shubha applies here as the Companion disagreement on a mukatib's status creates sufficient doubt to block the hadd of qadhf.

Accusing a Majusi Who Married His Mother Then Embraced Islam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qadhf for a Majusi convert

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute regarding hadd for qadhf of a Majusi who married his mother before Islam and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees pre-Islamic validity; Sahibayn see only post-Islam sin.

This passage presents a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school about how to treat a pre-conversion marriage among Majians. The question is whether someone who accuses a convert of zina for having married his mother before Islam should be punished for false accusation. The answer hinges on whether the original marriage is considered valid in Islamic law for the purpose of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
A Majusi man married his mother before converting to Islam. After conversion, someone accuses him of zina for that union. Determine if the accuser is liable for hadd of qadhf.
Key: the marriage was during pre-Islamic period.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa says the accuser is liable for hadd. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no hadd. Identify the two views.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam and Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the underlying basis
The dispute is built on whether the Majusi's marriage to his mother has the ruling of validity (hukm al-sihhah) among them according to Abu Hanifa, which would make the intercourse not zina, so the accusation is false.
Sahibayn do not give that marriage any legal effect; after Islam it is clearly zina.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If the accuser is subject to hadd, he receives 80 lashes. If not, he goes free. This is the practical consequence of the disagreement.
Hadd of qadhf is 80 lashes for free men.
5
Consider the tarjih
The text does not explicitly prefer one view, but often Abu Hanifa's view is considered stronger in such matters. Check later Hanafi works for the mufta bihi.
This passage references the Nikah chapter where the issue is discussed more fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْقَدَفَ مَجُوسِيًّا تَزَوَّجَ بِأَمِّهِ ثُمَّ أَسْلَمَ يُحَدُّ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَقَالَا لَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ وَهَذَا بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنْ تَزَوْجَ الْمَجُوسِيُّ بِالْمَحَارِمِ لَهُ حُكَمَ الصَّحَةُ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ عِندَهُ خِلَافًا لَهُمَا وَقَدْ مَرَّفِي النِّكَاحِ

And this is based on the issue that the marriage of a Majusi to his mahram has the ruling of validity among them, according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them. And this has passed in the Book of Nikah.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a Magian (Zoroastrian) who, before converting to Islam, married his own mother (which is permissible in the Magian religion). After becoming Muslim, someone accuses him of zina for having intercourse with his mother (since it is incest in Islam). Abu Hanifa holds that the accuser is subject to the hadd of qadhf, because among the Magians, such a marriage is considered valid, so the act is not zina from their perspective before Islam; hence the accusation is false. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) say no hadd on the accuser, because after Islam, the act is clearly zina, and the legal status before Islam is irrelevant. The disagreement stems from whether such a marriage among Magians is given legal effect. Abu Hanifa considers it valid as a contract among them (so the intercourse is not zina), while the two companions do not. The text notes this issue has already been discussed in the Nikah chapter.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majūsī): A Zoroastrian (Magian), a follower of the pre-Islamic Persian religion
محارم (maḥārim): Close relatives who are permanently prohibited for marriage
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; a fixed crime (hadd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The accuser is not subject to any hadd
C) The accused is stoned for zina

Hadd for Accusing a Magian Who Married His Mother: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qadhf of a Magian who married his mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether hadd for qadhf applies when the accuser accuses a Magian who married his mother before converting to Islam, and identify the basis of the disagreement (validity of the marriage).

Core Idea
A marriage invalid in Islam may be considered valid among non-Muslims for hadd rulings—Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute involving the fixed punishment (hadd) for false accusation of zina (qadhf). The case involves a Magian who married his own mother before converting to Islam. The ruling hinges on whether that marriage is considered valid among Magians, and thus whether an accusation of zina against him is false. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold opposing views, and we will analyze the legal reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the two rulings
Identify the scenario: a Muslim accuses a Magian who married his mother and then converted. According to Abu Hanifa, the accuser receives hadd; according to the Sahibayn, he does not.
2
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that the dispute rests on the validity of the Magian's marriage prior to conversion. Abu Hanifa considers it valid among them; the Sahibayn consider it invalid ab initio.
This principle is established in the earlier chapter on marriages of polytheists.
3
Analyze the application to qadhf
If the marriage is valid, the act between the Magian and his mother is not zina, so accusing him of zina is a false accusation (qadhf). If the marriage is invalid, the act is zina, and the accusation is true, so no hadd.
The hadd for qadhf only applies if the accusation is false.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The outcome is whether the accuser is punished with 80 lashes (Abu Hanifa) or not (Sahibayn).
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of the hadd punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) when the accused is a Magian who had married his own mother before converting to Islam. The ruling depends on the validity of the marriage among Magians. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a marriage is valid among them; therefore, the accusation of zina against this person is a false accusation (qadhf), and the accuser must receive the hadd punishment. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the marriage is invalid ab initio; thus, the sexual act between the Magian and his mother is considered zina, and accusing him of zina is truthful, so no hadd is applied. This dispute is built upon the earlier discussion in the chapter on marriages of polytheists.

Key Terms

حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes, including qadhf.

Hadd for Harbi with Aman Accusing a Muslim
Ruling with dalil: Harbi with aman liable for hadd al-qadhf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a harbi with aman is liable for hadd al-qadhf and explain the proof based on haqq al-'abd.

Core Idea
A harbi's aman binds him to respect Muslim rights; violating them triggers hadd.

This lesson examines a specific fiqh ruling: an enemy combatant (harbi) who enters Muslim lands with a safe conduct (aman) and then falsely accuses a Muslim of zina (qadhf) is subject to the hadd punishment. The proof is not from a specific text but from rational reasoning (istihsan) based on the implications of the aman contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize the act as qadhf (false accusation of zina) by a harbi with aman. State the ruling: hadd (80 lashes) is wajib.
The ruling is specific to qadhf, not all crimes.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) based on rational reasoning from the nature of aman. No direct Quran or hadith is cited.
Dalil aqli (rational evidence) is used here.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The harbi, by accepting aman, implicitly covenants to respect Muslims' rights. Qadhf violates a personal right (haqq al-'abd), so the hadd is applied to uphold that right.
The distinction between haqq al-'abd and haqq Allah is key.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes: hadd for zina (act) is not applicable to a harbi, but hadd for qadhf (accusation) is. The text follows the general rule.
Abu Yusuf's view is acknowledged but not relied upon here.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that hadd is imposed on the harbi for qadhf, consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ دَارَنَا بِأَمَانٍ فَقَذَفَ مُسْلِمًا حُدَّ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ حَقَّ الْعَبْدِ وَقَدِ الْتَزَمَ إِيفَاءَ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَلِأَنَّهُ طَمِعَ فِي أَنْ لَا يُؤْذَى فَيَكُونُ مُلْتَزِمًا أَنْ لَا يُؤْذِيَ.
And if a harbi (enemy combatant) enters our land with a guarantee of safety (aman) and then accuses a Muslim of zina, he is punished with hadd because it involves a right of a servant (of God) and he has committed himself to fulfilling the rights of the people, and because he hoped not to be harmed, so he is obligated not to harm others.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: an enemy combatant (harbi) who enters the Islamic territory with a safe conduct (aman) and then falsely accuses a Muslim of zina (qadhf) is liable for the hadd punishment of 80 lashes. The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the harbi, by seeking aman, implicitly agrees to respect the rights of the Muslims. Since qadhf violates a person's right (haqq al-'abd), and the harbi has committed to not causing harm, the punishment is necessary to uphold justice. This is unlike the fixed punishments that are purely rights of God (such as hadd for drinking wine), where the harbi might not be punished because the right of God may not be binding on non-Muslims. However, here the right of the individual is involved, so the hadd is enforced.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with the Islamic state.
أمان (aman): A guarantee of safety granted to a harbi temporarily allowing him to enter and stay in Dar al-Islam.
حق العبد (haqq al-‘abd): A right of an individual human being, as opposed to a right of God (haqq Allah).
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because qadhf violates a personal right of the Muslim, which the harbi has implicitly agreed to respect.
C) Because all non-Muslims are subject to hadd punishments.
D) Because the accuser is now a resident Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A harbi with aman is liable for hadd al-qadhf because the aman contract binds him to respect personal rights.

Single Hadd for Multiple Repeated Crimes and the Doctrine of Tadakhul
Inter-madhhab dispute on merging of hadd punishments for repeated crimes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on tadakhul (merging) of hadd punishments for repeated crimes, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the doctrine to scenarios of qadhf, zina, and shurb.

Core Idea
One hadd suffices for repeated same-type hudud crimes when the right of Allah dominates; different crimes do not merge.

This passage delves into the Hanafi doctrine of tadakhul, determining when a single hadd punishment can cover multiple offenses. It explains the reasoning based on the objective (deterrence) and the nature of the right involved (haqq Allah vs. haqq al-‘abd). The discussion highlights a key inter-madhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, particularly over qadhf (false accusation), offering a clear example of how legal principles translate into concrete rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by articulating the Hanafi rule: for multiple instances of the same crime (zina, shurb, qadhf), one hadd suffices for all repetitions.
This is the core of the doctrine of tadakhul.
2
Identify the scope of merging
Determine which crimes qualify: only those where the right of Allah is predominant and the crimes are of the same type. Crimes of different types do not merge.
The text explicitly excludes mixing different hudud.
3
Understand the rationale
The underlying objective is deterrence (inzijar). Since achieving deterrence with the first hadd creates doubt (shubha) about the need for additional punishment, the second is dropped.
This teleological reasoning (maqsad) is typical of Hanafi usul.
4
Recognize the Shafi'i counter-view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that for qadhf, since the right of the servant is predominant, merging does not apply if the accused person or the accusation differs.
This shows how classification of the crime (haqq Allah vs. haqq al-‘abd) leads to different outcomes.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Work through a scenario: a person repeatedly slanders the same individual. Hanafi: one hadd. Shafi'i: if each slander is about a different alleged act, multiple hadd.
This is the practical consequence of the differing views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ قَذَفَ اَوزَنَى اَوْ شَرِبَ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ فَحُدَّ فَهُوَ لِذَالِكَ كُلِهِ أَمَّا الْآخَرَان فَلانَّ الْمَقْصِدَ مِنْ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدِ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى الْإِنْزِ جَارُ وَ اِحْتِمَالُ حُصُولِهِ بِالْاَوَّلِ قَائِمٌ فَيَتَمَكَّنُ شُبْهَةُ فَوَاتِ الْمَقْصُودِ فِي الثَّانِي هَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَازَنَى وَقَذَفَ وَسَرِقَ وَشَرِبَ لِاَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنْ كُلَّ جِنْسِ غَيْرُ الْمَقْصُودِ مِنَ الْأَخَر فَلَا يَتَدَاخَلُ وَأَمَّا الْقَذْقُ فَالْمُغْلَبُ فِيْهِ عِنْدَنَا حَقُّ اللَّهِ فَيَكُونُ مُلْحَقًا بِهِمَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيِّ إِنِ اخْتَلَفَ الْمَقْذُوفَ اَوِ الْمَقْذُوقَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الزِّنَاءُ لَا يَتَدَاخَلُ لِاَنَّ الْمُغْلَبَ فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ عِنْدَهُ
ترجمہ کہا اگر کسی نے بار بار تہمت لگائی۔ یا خود زنا کیا یا شراب پی بعد میں اسے ایک بار حد لگائی گئی تو وہی حد سب کے لئے کافی ہوگی۔ اور دوسرے دونوں یعنی زنا اور شراب خوری کی صورت میں حق الہی کے واسطے حد قائم کرنے نے مقصود یہ ہوتا ہے کہ زانی اور شراب خور کو تنبیہ ہو۔ پس ایک بار ہی حد جاری کرنے سے اس مقصد کے حاصل ہو جانے کا احتمال ہے اور دوسری بار حد جاری کرنے میں اس مقصد کے فوت ہو جانے کا شبہ ثابت ہو گیا (۔کیونکہ اگر پہلی بار اسے تنبیہ حاصل ہوگئی تھی تو دوسری بارحد کا کیا مقصد تھا)۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے اگر زنا کیا اور چوری کی اور شراب بھی پی لی پھر ایک بار حد لگائی گئی تو یہ ایک حد کافی نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ہر جنس کی حد سے علیحدہ مقصد ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے حدود میں تداخل نہ ہوگا اور تہمت لگانے کی صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک حق اللہ عزوجل کو ترجیح حاصل ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی حد زنا اور شراب خوری سے بحق ہوگی اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ جن کو تہمت لگائی گئی یا جس کے ساتھ قذف کیا یعنی زنا کی تہمت الگ الگ ہو تو تداخل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک اس میں بندہ کا حق غالب ہے۔
He said: Whoever falsely accuses, or commits zina, or drinks (wine) multiple times, and then is punished (once), then it (the punishment) suffices for all of that. As for the other two (zina and drinking), because the objective of establishing the hadd – as a right of Allah the Exalted – is deterrence, and the possibility of its attainment by the first (punishment) exists, so a doubt arises about the loss of the objective in the second. This is contrary to the case when he commits zina, and false accusation, and theft, and drinking, because the objective of each category is different from the objective of another, so they do not merge. As for false accusation, according to us the right of Allah is predominant in it, so it is annexed to them (zina and drinking). And al-Shafi'i said: If the accused person is different, or the accusation is different – i.e., the zina alleged – they do not merge, because according to him the right of the servant is predominant in it. Translation: He said: If someone repeatedly falsely accuses, or commits zina, or drinks wine, and then is given one punishment, that punishment suffices for all. As for the other two (zina and shurb), because the objective of establishing the hadd as a right of Allah is to deter, and there is a possibility that this objective was achieved with the first, so a doubt arises about the attainment of the objective in the second. This is unlike the case if he commits zina, false accusation, theft, and drinking, because the objective of each category is different from the objective of the other, so they do not merge. As for false accusation, according to us the right of Allah is predominant in it, so it is annexed to the two (zina and shurb). And Imam Shafi'i said: If the accused person is different, or the accusation is different – i.e., the zina alleged – they do not merge, because according to him the right of the servant (individual) is predominant.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses the doctrine of tadakhul (merging) of hadd punishments. It distinguishes between multiple instances of the same crime and multiple different crimes. For crimes that are pure rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and have the same objective (deterrence), if a person commits the same crime multiple times (e.g., several acts of zina or several instances of drinking), one punishment suffices for all repetitions. The reasoning is that the purpose is deterrence, and once deterrence is achieved, there is doubt about whether additional punishment would serve any purpose; therefore, the hadd is not repeated. For different crimes (e.g., zina, qadhf, theft, drinking), each has a distinct objective, so one hadd does not cover another; they do not merge. Qadhf (false accusation) is treated similarly to zina and drinking because, in the Hanafi school, the right of Allah is predominant in qadhf, so it is annexed to them. Imam al-Shafi'i holds a different view: for qadhf, since the right of the servant (individual) is predominant, if the accused persons are different or the accusations differ, no merging occurs; each instance requires a separate hadd.

Key Terms
تداخل الحدود (tadākhul al-ḥudūd): The merging of punishments; one hadd suffices for multiple offenses of the same category where the right of God dominates.
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): The right of God; crimes where the punishment is fixed and not waivable by the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone commits zina three times and is then given the hadd punishment once:
A) He must receive three separate punishments.
B) One punishment suffices for all three acts.
C) He receives one punishment but must also perform tawba.
D) The punishment is split into three installments.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi doctrine of tadakhul merges hadd punishments for repeated same-type crimes where the right of Allah dominates, reflecting the maqasid of deterrence over retribution.

Ta'zir for Qadhf Against Non-Muhsan Victims
Ruling on qadhf of non-muhsan victims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when hadd for qadhf is replaced by ta'zir and apply the condition of ihsan for the victim.

Core Idea
Hadd requires muhsan; without it, false accusation still incurs ta'zir.

The hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) is reserved for protecting the honor of those who are fully qualified (muhsan). When the victim lacks one or more elements of ihsan—such as freedom, Islam, or marital consummation—the fixed penalty does not apply. However, false accusation remains a crime, and the judge imposes a discretionary punishment called ta'zir. This lesson examines which victims trigger ta'zir instead of hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the victim category
The act is qadhf (false accusation of zina). The victims are specified as slaves, slave-girls, umm walad (a slave who has borne a child to her master), and non-Muslims. List them.
All these categories lack one or more elements of ihsan: they are not free, not Muslim, or not both.
2
Determine hadd applicability
Check whether the victim is muhsan. For hadd to apply, the victim must be free, adult, Muslim, and have had lawful intercourse in a valid marriage. Since none of the listed victims meet this definition, the hadd obligation is prevented.
The lack of ihsan is the sole reason hadd is not obligatory.
3
Apply the ruling: ta'zir becomes wajib
Because the act is still a crime (jinayat qadhf) but hadd conditions are not met, the judge imposes ta'zir—a discretionary punishment. The Hanafi ruling states that ta'zir is wajib (obligatory) in such cases.
Ta'zir cannot exceed the lowest hadd (40 lashes for drinking) and is left to the judge's discretion.
4
Understand the legal basis (talil)
The underlying cause (illah) is the presence of a criminal act (qadhf) combined with the absence of the condition for hadd (ihsan). The absence of ihsan does not nullify the crime; it only changes the punishment from fixed to discretionary.
This is a form of istihsan: preserving the deterrent effect while respecting the conditions of hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَذَفَ عَبْدًا أَوْ آمَةً اَوْهُمْ وَلَدٍ وَ كَافِرًا بِالزِّنَاءِ عُزِرَلَانَّهُ جِنَايَةُ قَذْفِ وَقَدْ امْتَنَعَ وُجُوبُ الْحَدِ لِفَقْدِ الْإِحْصَانِ فَوَجَبَ التعزير
ترجمہ جس نے کسی غلام یا باندی یا اموال یا کافر کوزناکاری کی تہمت لگائی تو اس کو تحریر کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ سب جرم قذف کا ہے۔ مگر حد تقذف اس لئے نہیں لگائی جاسکتی ہے کہ وہ محسن نہیں ہے اس لئے تقریر واجب ہوئی۔
And whoever falsely accuses a slave, or a slave-girl, or an umm walad, or a non-Muslim, of zina, he is given ta'zir, because it is an offense of false accusation, but the obligation of hadd is prevented due to the lack of ihsan, so ta'zir becomes obligatory. Translation: Whoever falsely accuses a slave, or a slave-girl, or an umm walad, or a non-Muslim of zina, he will be given ta'zir. Because it is an offense of qadhf, but the hadd of qadhf cannot be imposed because they are not muhsan; therefore ta'zir is obligatory.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling when the victim of false accusation (qadhf) is not a muhsan person. The hadd punishment for qadhf (80 lashes) is only applicable when the victim is a free, adult, Muslim who has had lawful sexual intercourse in a valid marriage (i.e., is muhsan). For categories such as slaves, slave-girls, umm walad (a slave who has borne a child to her master), and non-Muslims, the hadd does not apply because they lack ihsan. However, the act of false accusation remains a crime (jinayat qadhf), so instead of the fixed hadd, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment called ta'zir. The severity of ta'zir is left to the judge's discretion, but it cannot reach the level of hadd. The underlying reason is that the hadd is reserved for protecting the honor of those who are fully qualified, while others are protected through ta'zir.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta‘zīr): A discretionary punishment imposed by the judge for crimes that do not have a fixed hadd or for which hadd conditions are not met.
إحصان (iḥṣān): A legal status required for the victim of qadhf to trigger the hadd; defined as being free, adult, Muslim, and having consummated a valid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person falsely accuses a Muslim slave of zina. According to the Hanafi school, what punishment applies to the accuser?
A) Hadd of 80 lashes.
B) Ta'zir.
C) No punishment because a slave cannot be a victim of qadhf.
D) The accuser must prove his allegation with four witnesses or receive hadd.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for qadhf requires the victim to be muhsan; otherwise, ta'zir is wajib.
